etc.


Merckt hier / dat d'Enghelsche somtijdts in plaetse van de prepositie to den
partijckel a ghebruycken; als I go a field. voornamentlijck voor verbalen; als
/ I go a fishing. I go a hunting etc.

Den Interjectie is even woordt dat even haestighe passie often ^laghte der sinnen
uytbeeldt; end is soodanigh als volght.

oh, alas. och armen / och lacy. woe. we. I pray thee. ey lieve. Ick bid u.
fie. foey etc.

Daer sijn oock andere reghelen en observatien / die ick tot beter perfectie en
volkomentheydt van dit werck / had konnen boorstellen / weghens accenten /
puncten / en andere dinghen / die hier niet eens aengheroert werden / om datse
in onse tale meesten deel met andere talen over-een komen / en dat mijn
voornemen alleenlijck is (als ick te voren verklaert hebbe) de breemdelinghen
hier sulcke regulen voor te stellen / waer door neffens de hulpe die sy in haer
eyghen tale hebben / sy tot de rechte kennisse en 't spreken onser Engelsche
tale moghen gheraken. 'T welcke ick tot hier toe ghedaen hebbe / met so veel
sorghe en u^^druckeliche^dt als mijnen tijdt end andere importante affairen
wild toelaten.

End so veel voor d'eerste often Etymologicale deel des Engelschen
School-meesters.

Het Tweede deel.
Cap. I. Van Syntaxis.
HEbbende tot hier toe vande pronuntiatie der letteren / vocaelen / Syllaben /
en woorden; mitsgaders de ghedeelten der sprake / so vele als den Engelsche
Etymology aengaet ghesproken: nu soude wy tot de regelen van Sijntaxis komen /
'twelcke is de behoorlijcke en rechte connexie end vast bindinghe van de
deelen der sprake aen en onder hun selven / na de rechte vorme end order.

Maer vermits ick onwilligh ben den leerling in sijn ghemoet met onnoodighe
reghelen te beswaren / often hem op te groote kosten in 't koopen van dit
boecksken te jaghen; wild ick well / dat het in even word aenghemerckt mochte
werden / dat de gene die de Duytsche often Latijnsche tale / en de reghelen van
Etymology gheleert heeft / en de woorden die hy in Enghelsch spreken moet kent
(waerinne hem den Dictionarium vele helpen kan) sal door sijn eygen
naturelijcke sprake / often de constructie van eenighe andere tale / oock weten
hoe hy sijne woorden inde Engelsche tale t'samen voeghen moet. Doch hy moet well
toe sien / dat hy sijne woorden niet nae de Duytsche often Latijnsche maniere
stelt / in welcke talen menighmael eerste in it spreeken en schrijven ghestelt
wordt dat inde constructie often verklaringhe lest komt. waer teghens wy in onse
Engelsche ta^e onse spraecke ghemeenlijcken meest na de order van de
constructie ordineren / niet anders als of school-jonghens even word na den
andere verbatim most verklaren / als.

1 He has well administered his office.

d. i. hy heeft well bedientsijn ampt.

hy heeft sijn ampt well bedient.

2 Th^^^ is need of diligence.

d. i. Daer is nood van naersticheyt.

daer is naersticheyt van noode.

3 He is worthy to be loved.

d. i. Hy is waerdigh te worden bemint.

Hy is waerdigh bemint te worden.

4 If mine honor remain whole and undamnified,

I regard not the damage of mine estate.

d: i. Indien mijn eer blijft geheel end onbeschadight: ick en pass niet op
de schade van mijn goet.

Als mijn eer gheheel end onbeschadight blijft; en pass ick op't verlies van
mijn goet niet,

Behoudende dat in het schrijven often spreken van relativen / sulcx als / whom,
which, what, whose, etc. ghebruycken wy de selve order in Syntaxis, als de
Duytsche en Latijnsche done / als in dese volghende sententien often redenen
ghefien kan werden.

1 Without delay I will do (what) thou have commanded.

datis:

Dat ghy bevolen hebt sal ick sonder vertoeven (often uytstel) volbrenghen.

2 Blessed is he (whose) transgression is forgiven and (whose) fin is covered.
Blessed is the man unto (whom) the Lord imputes not iniquity, and in (whose)
spirit there is no guile.

dat is:

Welgelucksalich is hy wiens overtredinghe vergheven is / end wiens sonde
bedeckt is. welgelucksalich is de mensche / dien de Here d'ongerechticheydt
met toe en rekent / en in wiens geeft geen bedroch en is.

Behalven oock dat wy in 't formeeren van dichten end rijmen de vrijicheyt der
Poeten gebruycken / die so veel op d'ordre des Syntaxis niet en letten / als
op de mate en loope haerer gedichten: en daerom stellen sy de woorden voor often
achter / na dat het best in de versen te pass homt.

Cap. II.
Maer om te bestuyten en all de boorgaende reghelen door oeffeninghe dienstich
te maken / en den leerling tot meerder perfectie in dese sake te brenghen / so
sal't hem ongetwijffelt profijtelijck zijn / dat hy sich in it lesen end van
buyten leeren der redenen / phrasen / spreeckwoorden / en andere volghende
discoursen deffent. Want daer mede sal hy sich behelpen niet alleen in 't
verstaen en kennisse der naemen van dinghen / end konsten; maer sal de taele
oock veel suyverder en eleganter spreecken. End vermits dat de vreese des
Heeren de eerste end voornaemste dingh is daer wy ons moeten in oeffenen: so
sal ick den leerling eenige stucken van Goddelijcke leeringe ten eersten
voorste len / waerinne het scer van noode is dat even ygelijck sich exerceert:
daerna sal ick de fin met verscheydene vermaeckelijcke redenen en spreucken
varverschen; end eyndelijck den leser eenige nuttelijcke 't famen / sprekingen
brieven / en andere gemeyne en noodwendighe stucken voor-houden.

Certain common scripture-places, and Christian speeches, very useful for the
practice of the former rules.
Eenighe ghemeyne Schrifruer-plaetsen, en Christelijcke redenen, seer dienstich
tot het ghebruyck der voorgaende regelen.
The some of the law of God, taken out of Math. 22.37, 38, 39, 40.
THou shall love the Lord thy God with all thine heart, and with all thy soul,
and with all thy understanding This is the first and great commandment. And
the second is like unto it, Thou shall love thy neighbor as thy self. On
these two commandments bang all the law and the prophers.

De somma des wets Godts, ghenomen uyt Matthew. cap. 22. verse. 37, 38, 39, 40.
GHy sult sief-hebben den Here uwen Godt met geheel uw' heart / end met
geheel uwe Ziele / end met geheel uw' verstandt Dit is het eerste end het
groot ghebodt. End het tweede desen gelijck is / ghy sult uwen naesten lief
hebben als u selven. Aen dese twee geboden hanght de gantsche wet end de
Propheeten.

The ten Commandments. Exodus 20. Deuteronomy. 5.
GOd spoke all these words and said: I am the Lord thy God, which, have brought
thee out af the land of Egypt, out of the house of bondage.

The first commandment. Thou shall have none other Gods before my face.

The second commandment. Thou shall make to thy self no graven image, nor any
likeness, either of any thing in heaven above, nor of any thing that is in earth
beneath, nor of any thing that is in the water under the earth: Thou shall not
bow down to them, nor serve them: for I am the Lord thy God, strong and jelous,
who visit the iniquity of the fathers upon the children, (even) to the third
and fourth generation of them that hate me; and show mercy to many thousands of
them that love me and keep my commandments.

The third commandment. Thou shall not take up the name of the Lord thy God in
vain or lightly: For the Lord will not hold him guiltless, nor leave him
unpunished, that takes his name in vain.

The fourth Commandment. Remember the Sabbath day, that thou keep it holy:
Six days shall thou labor, and do all thy work: but the seventh day is the
Sabbath of the Lord thy God, in it thou shall do no work, nor thy son, nor
thy daughter, nor thy servant, nor thy maid, nor thy cattle, nor the stranger,
which is within thy gates. For in six days the Lord made heaven and earth,
and the sea, with all that is therein, and he rested the seventh day: wherefore
the Lord blessed the Sabbath day, and hallowed it.

The fifth Commandment. Thou shall honor thy Father and mother, that thou
may live long upon the earth, and that it may go well with thee in the land,
which the Lord thy God shall give thee.

The sixth Commandment. Thou shall not kill.

The seventh Commandment. Thou shall not commit adultery.

The eighth commandment. Thou shall not steal.

The nineth Commandment. Thou shall bear no false witness against thy
neighbor.

The tenth Commandment. Thou shall not covet thy neighbors house, thou shall
not covet thy neighbors wife, nor his servant, not his maid, nor his ox, nor
his ass, nor any thing, which is thy neighbors.

De tien Gheboden. Exodus 20. Deuteronomy. 5.
GOdt sprack all dese woorden end seyde. Ick ben de Here uwen God die u uyt
Egypten landt uyt den diensthuyse gheleyt hebbe,

Dat eerste gebodt. Ghy en sult geen andere Goden voor mijn aenghesicht hebben.

Dat tweede gebod: Ghy en sult u geen beelden / noch geen gelijckenisse maken /
noch van 't gene dat boven inden Heme is / noch van 't gens dat onder op der
aerden is / noch van 't gene dat in it water onder der aerden is: En buygt u
voor die niet noch en dientse niet: want ick ben de Here uwe God / sterck end
gverigh die de misdaed der vaderen be soecke aen de kinderen / tot in dat derde
end vierde lid ded ghener die my haten; end do barmherticheydt aen veel
duysenden der ghener die my liefhebben / end mijn gheboden houden.

Dat derde gebod. Ghy en sult den name des Heeren uwes Gods niet te vergeefts
often lich^ veerdelijck ghebruycken: want de Here en sal hem niet onschuldigh
houden / noch onghestraft laten / die fijnen naem misbruyckt.

Dat vierde gebod. Zijt ghedachtigh des Sabbat daeghs / dat ghy dien heylighet:
Ses dagen sult ghy arbeyden / end all u werck done: maerve sevensien dagh is
den Sabbat des Heeren uwes Gods / dan sult gh^ gheen arbeyt done / noch u Sone
/ noch u dochter / noch u knecht / noch u dienst-maeght / noch u vee / noch de
vreemdelingh / die in uwe stadt poerten is. want in fes daghen heeft de Here
Hemal / end aerde gemaeckt / end de Zee met all dat daerin is / end hy
rustede den sebensten dagh: daerom segende de Here den Sabbath-dagh / end
heyligde den selven.

Dat vijfde gebod. Ghy fult u Vader end moeder eeren / op dat ghy langhe leeft
onder aerden / end dat het u well gae in den land / dat a de Here uwe God
geven fall.

Dat seste gebod. Ghy en sult niet dooden.

Dat sevenste gebod. Ghy en sult niet Echt-breken.

Dat achtste gebod. Ghy en sult niet steelen.

Dat negenste gebod. Ghy en sult gheen valsche ghe tuyghenisse spreken teghen
uwen naesten.

Dat tiende gebod. Ghy en sult niet begeeren uwes naesten huys / ghy en sult
niet begheeren uwes naesten wijf / noch sijn knecht / noch sijn dienst-maaght /
noch sijn offe / noch sijn esei / noch oock eenigh ding / dat uwen naesten
heeft.

The Lords prayer.
Our father, which art in heaven. Hallowed be thy name. Thy kingdom come. Thy
will be done on earth, as (it is) in heaven. Give us this day our daily bread.
And forgive us our debts, even as we forgive our debtors. And lead us not into
tentation, but deliver us from evil. For thine is the kingdom, the power, and
the glory, for ever. Amen.

Het ghebedt onses Heeren.
ONse Vader / die daer zijt in de Hemelen. Geheyligt werde uwe name. Vwe rijcke
kome. Vwe will geschiede / op der aerden / als in den Hemel. Geeft ons heden
ons dagelijcx broot. End vergeeft ons onse schulden / ghelijck wy vergeven
onse schulde naeren. End en leydt ons niet in versoeckinghe; maer verlost ons
van den quaden. Want u is dat tijck / de kracht / end de Heerlijckheyt / in
der eeuwigheyt, Amen.

The Commission given by Christ to his Apostles Math. 28.18, 19.
Go ye therefore, and teach all nations; baptising them in the name of the
Father, and of the son, and of the holy Ghost: Teaching them to observe all
things whatsoever I have commanded you: and lo, I am with you always, (even)
unto the end of the world.

Het bevel door Christum aen sijn Apostelen gegeven Mar. 28.18, 19.
GAet dan henen / en onderwijst all de volckeren / de selve doopende in den
name des Waders / end des foons / end des He^ligen Geests leerende haer
onderhouden alles wat ick u geboden hebbe; end fiet / ick ben met u lieden
all de dagen / tot de voleyndiughe der werelt.

The institution of the holy supper of our Lord, taken out of 1. Cor. 11.23.
etc. and 1. Co. 10.16, 17.
FOr I have received of ye Lord that which also I delivered unto you, that ye
Lord Jesus in the same night in which he was betrayed, took bread: And when he
had given thanks, ^e brak^ it, and said, Take, eat; this is my body, which is
broken for you: this do in remembrance of me. After the same manner also he
took the cup when he had supped; and said, This cup is the new testament in my
blood; this do ye, as often as ye drink it, in remembrance of me. For as often
as ye eat this bread, and drink this cup, ye do show the Lords death till
he come. wherefore whosoever shall eat this bread, and drink this cup of the
Lord unworthily; shall be guilty of the body and blood of the Lord.

But let a man examine himself, and so let him eat of that bread, and drink of
that cup. For he that eats and drinks unworthily, eats and drinks
damnation to himself, not difcerning the Lords body.

The cup of blessing which we bless, is it not a Communion of the blood of
Christ? The bread which we break, is that not a Communion of the body of
Christ? For (it is) one bread, (so) we many are one body: seeing we are all
partakers of one bread.

De insettinghe des Heylighen Avontmaels onses Heerengenomen uyt 1. Cor 11.23.
etc. en 1. Cor. 10.16, 17.
WAnt ick hebbe van den Here ontfangen / 'tgene ick oock u overge gheven hebbe
/ dat de Here Jesus in den nacht in welcken hy verraden wiert / het broot name
End als hy gedanckt had / brack hy 't / end seyde / nemet / Etet; dat is
mijn lichaem dat voor u ghebroken wordt: doet dat tot mijner ghedachtenisse.
Desgelijcx nam hy oock den drinck beker nae het eten des Abontmaels; end se^de
/ dese drinck-beker is het Nieuwe testament in mijnen bloede; doet dat / so
dickwils als ghy dien sal drincken / tot mijner gedachtenisse. Want so
dickwils als ghy dit broodt sult eten / end dese drinck-beker sult drincken /
so verkondight ghy den doot des Heeren / tot dat hy komt. So dan wie
onweerdelick dit broot eet / often den drinck-beker des Heeren drinckt / die sal
schuldich zijn aen het lichaem end bloedt des Heerrn.

Maer laet de mensche beproeve hem selven / end eete also van het broot / end
dr^ncke van den drinck-beker. Want die onweerdelijck eet end drinckt / die eet
end drinckt hem self even oordeel / niet onderscheydende het lichaem des Heeren.

De drinck-beker der danck-segginge / dien wy feghenen / is die niet even
ghemeynschap des bloeds Christi? Het broot dat wy breken / is dat niet even
ghemeynschap des lichaems Christi? Want even broodt (is het / so) zijn wy vele
even lichaem: dewijle wy all eenes broodts deelachtigh zijn.

Rules of Church Discipline, Matthew. 18.15. etc.
MOre-over if thy brother has trespassed against thee, go and tell him his
fault between thee and him allone: if he hears thee, thou have gained thy
brother. But if he hears thee not, then take with thee one or two more, that
in the mouth of two or three witnesses every word may be established. And if
be give them no hearing, then tell it to the church: and if he also give the
church no hearing, then let him be unto thee as an heathen man, and a publican.
Verily I say unto you, whatsoever ye shall bind on earth, shall be bound in
heaven: and whatsoever ye shall loose on earth, shall be loosed in heaven,
Again I say unto you, that if two of you shall agree on earth, as touching any
thing, that they shall ask; it shall be don for them of my father which is in
heaven. For where two or three are gathered together in my name, there am I in
the midst of them.

Regelen van Kerckelijcke disciplyne. Matthew. 18 15. etc.
VOorders indien uw' Broeder tephen u ghesondicht heeft / gaet he^en end
bes^^a hem ^ussghen u end hem alleen: indien hy u hoort / so hebt ghy uwen
brooder ghewonnen. Maer indien hy u niet en hoort / so neemt noch even of twee
met u: op dat in den mont van twee often dry ghetuyghen all woort bes^ae. End
indien hy de selve gheen gehoor en geeft / so feght het der geme^nte end
indien hy oock der gemeynte geen ghehoor en geeft / so z^^h u als de heyden
end de tollen^er Voorwaer segge ick u al wat ghy op der aerden binden sult /
sal in den Hemel gebonden wesen: end al wat ghy op der aerd^n ontbinden sult;
sal in den Hemel ontbonden wesen. Wederom segghe ick u / indien daer twee van u
t'famen stemmen op der aerden / over eenighe fake die sy fouden mo hen
begheeren / dat die haer sa^ ^eschieden van mijnen Vader die in de Hemelen is.
Want waer twee often dry vergadert zijn in mijnen name daer ben ick in 't midden
van haer.

The 12 articles of the Catholic Christian faith.
I Believe in God the Father, the Almighty maker of heaven and earth. And in
Jesus Christ his only begotten son our Lord: which was conceaved of the holy
Ghost, born of the virgin Mary; who suffered under Pontius Pilate, was
crucified, dead, and beried, descended into hell. The third day he arose again
from the dead, ascended into heaven, (and is) sitting at the right hand of God,
the father Almighty, from whence he shall come, to judge the quick and the
dead. I believe in the holy Ghost. I believe an holy Cha^holike Christian
church the Communion of Saints: forgivenes of sins: resurrection of the flesh:
and life everlasting.

De 12 Artyckelen des alghemeynen Christelijcken gheloofs.
ICk ghe^oove in Godt den Vader / den Almachtighen Schepper des Hemels end der
aerden. End in Iesum Christum sijnen eenich-geborenen Sone onsen Here: die
ontfanghen is van den Heyligen Gheest / gheboren uyt de Maghet Maria; die
gheleden heeft onder Pontio Pilato / is ghekruyst / ghestorven / end begraven
/ neder-ghedaelt tee hellen. Ten derden daghe weder op gestaen van de dooden /
opghevaren ten Hemel / sittende ter rechter-handt Gods / des Almachtighen
Vaders / van waer hy komen sal / om te oordeelen de levendighe end de dooden.
Ick gheloove in den Heylighen Gheest. Ick geloove even Heylighe alghemeyne
Christelijcke Kercke: ghemeenschap der Heylighen: verghevinghe der sonden:
opslandinge des vleeschs end eeuwig leven.

The Confession of faith composed in the Council of Nice, in the 325 year after
the birth of Christ.
WE believe in one God, the father Almighty, maker of heaven and earth, and of
al things visible and invisible: and in one Lord Jesus Christ, the only
begotten son of God, begotten of the father before all worlds, God of God,
light of light, very God of very God, begotten and not made, (being) of one
substance with the father, by whom all things were made; who for us men, and
for our salvation, came down from heaven, and was incorporate by the holy
Ghost in the virgin Mary, and was made man, and was crucifi^d also for us under
Pontius Pilate, who suffered and was buried, and the third day he rose again
according to the scriptures, and ascended into heaven, and fitteth on the right
hand of the father. And that he shall come again with glory to judge (both)
the quick and the dead, whose kingdom shall have none end. And we believe in
the holy Ghost the Lord and giver of life, who proceeds from the father and
the son, who with the father and the son together is worshipped and glorified,
who spoke by the Prophets. And we believe one holy Catholic and Apostolic
church; we acknowledge one baptism for the remission of sins. And we look for
the resurrection of the dead, and the life of the world to come.

Belijdenisse des Geloofs, gestelt in het Concilium van Niceen, in den jare na
Christi geboorte 325.
WY ghelooven in eenen Godt / den Almachtighen Vader / Scheppet des Hemels end
der aerde / end aller dinghen sienlijcke / end onsienlijcke: end in eenen
Here Iesum Christum / den eenich gebooren sone Gods / gebooren uyt den Vader
voo^ all eeuwen / Godt uyt Godt / licht uyt licht / waerach tigh God uyt
waerachtigh Godt / geboren end niet ghemaeckt / van 't selve wesen met de
Vader / door welcke all dinghen gemaeckt zijn; die om ons menschen end om
onse Salicheydt is nederghekomen uyt den Hemel / end vleesch gheworden is uyt
den Heyligen Geeft inde Maget Maria / end even Mensch is geworden / die voor
ons oock gecruyciget is onder Pontius P^latus. Die gheleden heeft / end
begraven is / end ten derden daghe opghestaen is na Scriften / end opghevaren
is ten Hemel / end sit ter dechter-handt des Vaders. End dat hy sal weder
komen metheerliche dt om te oordeelen de levende end de doode / wiens rijcke
geen eynde en sal hebben. End wy geloove inden Herlighen Ghrest / den Here
end ghever des levens / die van den Vader end den Sone uytgekomen is / wie 't
samen met den Vader end den Sone ghedient end gheheerlicht is / die
ghesproken heeft door de Propheten End wy gheloven eene Herlighe alghemeyne
end Apostolische Kercke. Wy belijden eenen doop tot vergevinghe der sonden.
End we verwachten de opstandighe der deoden / end het leven der toekomende
eeume.

The form of Creed, and Confession of Athanasius Bishop of Alexandria, written
in the 333 year after Christ's birth.
Whosoever will be saved, before all things it is necessary for him, that he
hold the Catholic faith: which faith whosoever does not keep whole and
undefiled, without doubt he shall perish everlastingly.

And the Catholic faith is this: That we worship one God in Trinity, and
Trinity in unity; without confounding ye persons, or dividing the essence and
substance For there is one person of the father, another of the son, and
another of the holy Ghost: but the father the son, and ye holy Ghost have one
godhead, glory equal, and Majesty coeternall. Such as the father is, such is
also the son, and such is the holy Ghost. The father is uncreated, the son is
uncreated, and the holy Ghost is uncreated. The father is incomprehensible, the
son is incomprehensible, and the holy Ghost is incomprehensible.

The father is eternal, the son is eternal; and the holy Ghost eternal. And
yet they are not three eternals, but one eternal: as also not three
incomprehensibles, not three uncreated: but one uncreated and one
incomprehensible. So likewise the father is almighty, the son almighty and the
holy Ghost almighty: and yet they are not three almighties, but one almighty.
So also the father is God, the son God, and the holy Ghost God: and yet they
are not three Gods, but one God. So likewise the father is Lord, the son Lord,
and the holy Ghost Lord: and yet there are not three Lords but one Lord. For
like as we be compelled by the Christian verity, to call every person by
himself God and Lord: so are we forbidden by the Catholic faith, to
acknowledge three Gods or (three) Lords. The father is made of none, neither
created, nor begotten; the son is of the father allone, not made, nor created,
but begotten: the holy Ghost is of the father, and the son; neither made, nor
created, nor begotten, but proceeding. So that there is one father, not three
fathers, one son, not three sons; one holy Ghost not three holy Ghosts. And in
this Trinity there is neither first nor last, nor greatest nor least: but the
whole three persons have equal eternity, and are in all things coequal. So that
in all things as is aforesaid, the unity in Trinity, and Trinity in unity is to
be worshipped. He therefore that will be saved, must thus think of the Trinity.

Furthermore it is necessary to everlasting salvation, that he also believe
rightly the incarnation of our Lord Jesus Christ. For the right faith is, that
we believe and confess, that our Lord Jesus Christ the son of God, is God and
man. God of the substance of the father, begotten beforeal world; and man of
the substance of his mother, born in the world: perfect God, and perfect man;
having a reasonable soul, and humane flesh. Equal to the father as touching his
godhead, inferior to the father touching his manhood: who although he be God
and man, yet is he not two, but one Christ; One, not by conversion of the
godhead into flesh, but by taking of the manhood into God; one altogether, not
by confusion of substance, but by unity of person. For as the reasonable soul
and flesh is one man: so God and man is one Christ, who suffered for our
salvation, descended into hell rose again the third day from the dead, he
ascended into heaven, sits on the right hand of God the father almighty:
from whence he shall come to judge the quick and the dead.

At whose coming al men shall rise again with their bodies, and give account
for their own works: and they that have don good, shall go into life
everlasting; but they that have don evil, into everlasting fire.

This is the Catholic faith: which if a man believes not faithfully and
certainly, he cannot be saved.

Gheloofs-forme, end bekentenisse Athanasij Bisschop van Alexandrien,
geschreven in it jaer nae Christi geboorte 333.
SO wie will Saligh zijn / dien is voor all dingh noodigh / dat hy het algemeyn
gheloove houde: het welcke gheloove so wie niet gheheel end ongeschent en
bewaert / die sal sonder twijffel eeuwighlijck verdedven.

End het algemeyne geloove is dit: dat wy den eenighen Godt inde dryheydt /
end de dryheyt in de eenigheyt eeren; sonder de persoonen te vermengen / often
het wesen end substantie te deylen. want het is even ander persoon des Vaders /
even ander des soons / end even ander des H. Geefts: Maer de Vader / sone end
Heyligen Geest hebben even Godtheyt / gelijcke eere / end ghelijcke eeuwighe
eetlijckheydt Hoedanigh de Vader is foodanigh is oock de Sone; foodanigh is
oock de Heylight Gheest. De Vader is ongheschapen / de Sone is ongeschapen /
end de Heyligen Geest is ongeschapen. Onmetelijck is d^ Vader / onmetelijck is
de Sone / end onmetelijck is de Heyligen Geest.

De Vader is eeuwigh

De sone is eeuwigh end de He^lighen Gheest is eeuwigh. Nochtans en zijn 't
niet dry eeuwighe / maer even eeuwigh: ghelijck oock niet dry onme telijcke /
noch dry ongheschapene: M^er even ongheschapen end even onmetelijck. Desgelijcx
is de Vader almachtigh / de Sone almachtigh / en de H. Gheest almachtigh: end
nochtans en zijn 't niet dry almachtige / maer even almachtigh. A^soo oock is de
Vader Godt / de Sone Godt / end de H. Geest Godt: end nochtans zijn 't niet
dry Goden / maer het is even Godt. Alsoo is de Vader Here / de Sone Here /
end de Heylige Gheest Here: End nochtans zijn 't niet dry Heeren; maer even
Here. Want gelijck wy door de Christen-waerheydt bedwonghen worden / eenen
yegelijcken per: soon by-sonder / Godt end Here te noemen: Also is ons oock
door het alghemeyn gheloove verboden dry Goden often Heeren te bekennen. De Vader
en is van niemandt gemaeckt / noch gheschapen / noch gheghener eert / de Sone
is vanden Vader alleen / niet ghemaeckt / noch gheschapen / maer geghenereert:
de Heylige Geest is vanden Vader end den Sone / met ghemaeckt / noch
gheschapen / noch ghegenereert / maer uytghekomen. So is daer dan even Vader /
niet dry Vaders; even Sone / niet dry Sonon; even H Geest / niet dry H. Gheesten.
End in dese dryheydt en is niet eerst / noch laetst / niet meest noch minst:
maer de ganische dry personen hebben gelij ke eeuwigheyt / end sy ben selven
allesins gelijck. So dat alomme ghelijck nu gheseyt is / de eenheyt inde
dryheydt / end de dryheyt inde eenheyt zy te eeten. Daerom so wie will Saligh
zijn / die moet aldus van de dryvuldigheyt gevoelen.

Doorts het is tot de eeuwige Saligheyt noodigh / dat hy oock de
mensch-werdinghe onses Heeren Jesus Christi trouwelijck gheloove. Want het
rechte geloove is / dat wy gelooven end belijden / dat onse Here Jesus
Christus Godts Sone / zy Godt end mensche. God uyt de substantie des Daders /
voor all tijden ghegenereert: end mensch / uyt de substantie fijns Moeders /
in den tijdt geboren: volkomen Godt end volkomen mensche; hebbende even
verstandighe Ziele / end menschelijck vleesch. Den Dader gelijck na de
Godtheyt / minder dan de Dader nae de menscheyt: de welcke hoe well hy Godt is
end mensche / so is hy nochtans niet twee / maer even Christus: Even / niet
door veranderinge der Godtheyt in het vleesch / maer door de aenneminghe der
menscheyd^ in Godt; even al t'famen / niet door de vermenginghe der substantie /
maer door de eenheydt des persoons Want gelijck de verstandige Ziele end het
vleesch even mensche zijn: also is Godt end de me^sche even Christus. De welcke
gheleden heeft om onser Salicheyts wil^s / nederghedaelt is ter hellen / ten
derden daghe weder opghestaen van den dooden / opgheklommen ten Hemel / sit ter
rechter-handt Godts des Vaders Almachtigh: van daer hy komen sal om te
oordeelen de levendige end de doode.

Tot des welckes komste all menschen sullen weder opstaen met hare lichamen
end van hare e^gene wercken reeckenschap gheven: end die goet gedaen hebben /
sullen in het eeuwige leven gaen / maer die quaet ghedaen hebben / in it eeuwige
vyer.

Dit is het algemeyn gheloove: het welck so wie niet trouwelijck end vast en
ghelooft / die en sal niet moghen Salich zijn.

The 38 and 39 chapters of the book of Job: and a part of the 40 and 41.
chapters.
THen the Lord answered Job out of the whirlewind, and said, who is he that
darkeneth counsel by words without knowledge? Gird up now thy loins like a
man, and I will demand of thee, and teach thou me. where wast thou when I laid
the foundations of the earth? declare if thou have understanding. who has laid
the measures thereof, if thou know it? or who has stretched the line upon
it? where upon are the foundations thereof fastened? of who laid the corner
stone thereof? when the morning stars sang joyfully together, and all the
children of God shouted for joy.

Or who shut up the sea with doors, when it brake forth as if it had issued out
of the womb? when I made the cloud the garment: thereof, and thick darkness a
swadling-band for it: when I brake up for it my decreed place, and set bars and
doors, and said, hitherto shall thou come, but no further: and here shall he
set himself against the pride of thy waves.

Have thou commanded the morning since thy days? have thou caused the
dayspring to know its place, that it might take hold of the ends of the earth,
that the wicked might be shaken out of it? that it should be turned as clay to
the seal, and they stand as a garment. And that from the wicked their light is
withheld, and the high arm shall be broken. Have thou entered into the
springs of the sea? and have thou walked in the search of the depth? Have the
gates of death been opened unto thee? and have thou seen the doors of the
shadow of death?

Have thou perceaved the breadth of the earth? declare if thou know it all.
Where is the way where the light dwells? and (as (...)) darkness, where is the
place thereof? that thou should, bring it to the bound thereof, and that
thou should know the paths to the house thereof? Thou know it, for thou
wast then borne: and thy days are many in number.

Have thou entered into the treasures of the snow? and have thou seen the
treasures of the hail, which I have reserved against the time of trouble,
against the day of battle and war?

Where is the way where the light is parted, and the east wind scatters it
self upon the earth? who has divided a watercourse for the overflowing of
waters: and a way for the lightening of thunder? To cause it to rain on the
earth, where no man is; on the wilderness, wherein there is no man; to satisfy
the desolate and wast ground, and to cause the bud of the tender he^b to spring
forth. Has the rain a father? Or who brings forth the drops of the dew?

Out of whose womb comes the ice? and who gendereth the boary frost of
heaven? The waters are hid as with a stone, and the face of the deep is frozen.

Can thou bind the sweet influences of Pleiades, or loose the bands of
Orion? Can thou bring forth Mazzaroth in his season, or can thou guide
Arcturus with his son^? Know thou the ord^nances of heaven: or can thou
set the dominion thereof on the earth? Can thou lift up thy voice to the
clouds, that abundance of waters may cover thee? Can thou send forth
lightenings, that they may go and say unto thee, behold, Here we are?

Who has put wisdom in the inward parts? or who has given understanding to
the mind? who can number the clouds in wisdom? or who can stay the bottles of
heaven? when the dust grows into hardness, and the clods cleave fast together.

Will thou hunt the prey for the old lion ^or fill the appetite of the young
lions? when they couch in their dens, and abide in the covert to lie in wait?
who provideth for the raven his food, when his young ones cry unto God, when
they wander for lack of meat?

Know thou the time when the wild goats of the rock bring forth? Have thou
marked when the hindes do calve? Can thou number the months which they
fulfill? and know thou the time when they bring forth? when they bow
themselves, they with Splitting bring forth their young ones, they cast our
their sorrows. Their young ones are in good liking, they grow up with corn:
hey go forth, and return not unto them.

Who has sent out the wild ass free: and who has loosed the bands of the
wild ass? whose house I have made the wilderness, and the barren land his
dwellings. He scorneth the multitude of the city, neither regards he the
crying of the driver. The raunge of the mountains is his pasture, and he
searches after every green thing.

Will the unicorne be willing to serve thee, will he abide by thy crib? Can
thou bind the unicorne with his band in the sorrow: will he barrow the
valleys for thee? will thou trust him because his strength is great? and will thou leave thy labor to him? will thou believe him that he will bring home thy
seed, and gather (it) into thy barn?

Gave thou the goodly wings unto the peacocks, or the feathers unto the
Stork, and unto the ostrich? That she leaves her eggs in the earth, and
warmeth them in the dust, and forgets that the foot may crush them, and that
the beasts of the field may break them. She hardens her self against her
young ones, as if they were not hers; her labor is in vain because she is
without fear. Because God has deprived her of wisdom, and has not imparted
to her understanding, when it is time, she lifts up her self on high: she
scorneth the horse and his rider.

Can thou give y horse strength? Can thou cloth his neck with thunder?
Can thou make him afraid as a grasshopper? the glory of his nostrils is a
terror. He paweth in the valley, and rejoices in his strength: and he goes
on to meet the armed men. He mocketh at fear, and it not affrighted; neither
turns he back from the sword. The quiver ratleth against him, the glittering,
iron of the pike and the lance. He swalloweth the ground with fiercenes and
rage: and he beleiveth not that it is the sound of the trumpet. He says among
the trumpets ha ha; and he smells the battle afar off, the thunder of the
captains and the shouting.

Does the hawke fly by thy understanding, and stretch her wings toward the
south? Is it at thy command that the Eagle does mount upon high, and that he
makes his nest on high? He dwells and abides on the rock, upon the crag of
the rock, and the strong place. From thence he seeks the prey: his eyes
behold a far off. His young ones also suck up blood: and where the slain are
there is he.

Behold now Behemoth which I have made with thee, he eats gras as an ox. Lo
now, his strength is in his loins, and his force is in the navell of his
belly. when he pleases his tail is like a cedar: the sinews of his shame are
wrapped together. His bones are as strong bras, his bones are like bars of iron.
He is a chief part of the ways of God: he that made him, can make his sword
to approach unto him. Because the mountains bring him forth ^od: therefore all the beasts of the field play there. He lies under the shady trees, in the
covert of the reeds, and f^rs. The shady trees cover him, each one with his
shadow: the willows of the brook compass him about. Behold he does violence to
the river and hastes not: he trusts that he can draw up Jordan into his
mouth. Can men take him before his eyes? can men pierce him through the nose
with snars?

Can thou draw out Levia than with an hook, or his tongue with a cord which
thou let down? Can thou put an hook into his nose, or boar his jawe
through with a thorn? will he make many supplications unto thee? will he
speak soft words unto thee? w^ll he make a covenant with thee, will thou take
him for a servant for ever? will thou play with him as with a bird? or will thou bind him for thy maidens? Shall the companions make a banquet of him?
shall they part him among the Merchants? Can thou fill his skin with barbed
irons: or his head with a fishers spear? Lay thine hand upon him, remember the
battle, do no more. Behold his hope shall fail; shall he not be cast down at
the sight of him? None is so fierce that dare stir him up: who then is he that
will stand before me? who has prevented me that I should repay him?
whatsoever is under the whole heaven is mine. I will not conceal his parts,
nor the relation of his power, nor the comelynes of his proportion, who can
discover the face of his garment? or who can come to him with his double
bridle? who can open the doors of his face? Round about his teeth is terror.
His strong scales are very excellent; each one shut up together at with a close
seal. One is so near to an other, that the air cannot come between them. They
are joined one to another, they stick together, that they cannot be fundered.
Every one of his neesings makes a light to shine, and his eyes are like the
eye lids of the morning. Out of his mouth go burning lamps and sparks of fire
leap out. Out of his nostrils goes smoke, at out of a seething pot or caldron.
His breath would kindle coals, and a stame goes out of his mouth. In his neck
lodges strength, and sorrow it self leapeth for joy before him. The flakes of
his flesh are joined together: every one is firm in him, it cannot be moved.
His heart is as firm as a stone, yea as hard as a piece of the nether
millstone. when he raises up himself the mighty are afraid by reason of his
breakings through, they purify themselves. If any one touch him with the
sword, that shall not hold: the spear, the dart, nor the habergeon. He
esteems iron as straw, and steel as rotten wood. The arrow cannot make him
fly: sling-stones are turned with him into stubble. Darts are counted as
stubble: and be laugheth at the shaking of the spear. Sharp Sheards are under
him: he spreads himself, on sharp pointed (things) as upon mire. He makes
the deep to boil like a pot: he makes the sea like a pot of ointment. He
makes the path to shine after him; one would think the deep to be hoarie. Upon
earth there is not his like: Who is made to be without fear. He beholds all
high things: be is a king over al young proud beasts.

Den 38 en 39 capittelen des boecks Jobs: oock even gedeelte des 40 en 41
capittelen.
DAerna antwoorde de Here Job uyt den onweder / en se^de, wie is hy / die den
raedt verduystert met woorden sonder wetenschap? Gordt nu als even man uwe
lendenen; so sal ick u vragen / end onderricht my.

Waer waert ghy / do ick de aerde grondede? gheeft het te kennen / indien ghy
kloeck van verstande zijt. Wie heeft-hare maten gheset indien ghy weet het?
often wie heeft over haer den richt-snoer ghetrocken? waer op zijn hare gront
vesten neder-ghesoncken? often wie heeft haren hoeck-steen gheleght? Do de
morgen-sterren 'tsamen vrolick songen / end all de kinderen Godts juycheden.

Often wie heeft de Zee met deuren toeghesloten / doe^e uytbrack als oftse uyt
de baermoeder voortquam? Do ick de wolcke tot hare kleedinghe stelde; end de
donckerhe^dt tot haren windel-doeck: do ick voor haer mijn besluyte plaetse
doorbrack / end settede grendelen / end deuren / end serde / Tot hier toe
sul^ ghy komen / en niet voorder: end hier sal hy sich stel en teghen den
hoochmoet uwer golven.

Hebt ghy van uwe daghen den morghen-stont gheboden? hebt ghy den dagheraet
fijne plaetse ghewesen? op dat hy de e^uden der aerde vat^en soude; dat de
godtloose uyt haer uytgheschuddet sonden worden? dat sy verandert soude worden
/ gelijck segel-lijm; end sy ghestelt worden / als even kleedt. End dat vande
godloose haer licht gheweerdt word; end den hooghen arm word gebroken. Zijt
ghy gekomen tot aen de oorsprongen der Zee? end hebt ghy in het onderste des
afgconts ghewandelt? Zijn u de poorsen des doots ontdecket? End hebt ghy
ghesien de poorsen van de schaduwe des doodis?

Zijt ghy niet u verstant ghekomen tot aen de breedten der aerde? geeft het te
kennen / indien ghy dit alles weet. Waer is de wegh daer het licht wont? end
de duysternisse waer is hare plaetse? dat ghy dat brengen soudt jot sijne pale
/ end dat ghy mercken soudt de paden sijns Huys? Ghy weet'et / want ghy waert
do gheboren: end uwe daghen zijn vere in ghetale.

Zijt ghy ghekomen tot de si hat kameren der sneeuw? end hebt ghy de
schat-kameren des Hag^ is ghesien / dien jest ophoude tot ben tijdt der
ben^u^he vt / tot de dach des s^^^ts / end der oorloghe?

Waer is de wegh daer het light verdeelt wordt; end de co^^en-windt sich
versiro (...) der aerde? wie beelt voor den s^ort reghen eenen water* ^op uri^
end eenen wegh voor het weerlicht der dondeten? Om te reghenenop het lant /
daer niemant en is op de woes^ijne / daer in geen mensche er is. Om het woes^e
end bet verwoestede te verfadighen: en^ om het uytspruytsel der gras
scheutkens te done wassen. Heeft de ^eghen eenen Dader? often wie baert de
druppelen des dauws?

D^^ wiens burck komt het ^s voort? end wie baert den rijm des Hemels? Als met
eenen steen verberghen haer de wateren: end het black des af-gronis wort om
vat.

Kondt ghy de lief lickheden van het seven ghesiernte binden / often de
s^ringhen Orions los maken? kondt ghy de Mazzaroth voort brengen in haren tijt
end den waghen met fijne soonen erden? weet ghy de ordinantien des Hemels /
often kent ghy de heerschapp^e des selven op de aerde besiellen? kont ghy uwe
s^emme tot de wolcken opheffen; op dat even over-vloedt van water u bedecke?
kont ghy de blixemen uyt laten / datse henen baren / end tot u segghen / siet
hier zijn wy?

Wie heeft de wijsheydt in it binnenste gheset? often wie heeft den sin het
verstan^ ghegeven? wie kan de wolken met wijsheyt sel'en? end wie kan de
flesschen des Hemels nederleggen? Als het s of door, ooten is tot vas icheyt /
end de kluyten 't famen kleben?

^ult ghy voor den ouden Leeuw roof jaghen? of de graegheyt den jonge Leeuwen
vervullen? Als sy neder-bucken in haer holen end in den kuyl sitten / ter
loeringhe. Wie bereydt de cave haren kost / a^s hare jonghen tot Godt schreuwen
/ als sy dwalen / om datter geen Eten en is?

Weet ghy den tijt van het baren der steen-geyten? hebt ghy waer genomen den
arbeyt der hinden? Sult ghy de maenden tellen die sy vervullen? end weet ghy
den tij^ van haer baren? Als sy haer krommen / hare jongen met verspl^tinge
voort-brengen / hare smerten uytwerpen? Hare jongen worden kloeck / worden
groot door het koorn / sy gaen uyt / end en keeren niet weder tot de se^ve.

Wie heeft den Woudt-Gzel vry henen ghesonden? end wie heeft de banden des
wilden Ezels ghelost? Dien ick de wildernisse tot sijn Huys bestelt hebbe /
end het siltighe tot sijne wooninghen. Hy belacht het ghewoel der Stadt / het
menigerley getier des drijvers en hoort hy niet. De uytspeuringe der berghen is
sijne weyde: end hy soeckt allerley groensel na.

Sal den eenhoorn u willen dienen? sal hy vernachten aen uwe kribbe? Sult ghy
den eenhoorn met sijn touw aen de voren binden? sal hyde leechten u eggen? sult
ghy op hem vertrouwen / om dat sijne kracht groot is? en^ sult ghy uwen arbeyt
op hem laeten? Sult ghy hem gelooven / dat hy u zaet sal weder brengen / end
vergaderen tot uwen dorsch-vloer?

Sijn van u de verheugelicke vleughelen der pauwen? often de vederen des
Oy-vaers / end des Struys voghels? Dat sy hare eyeren inde aerde laet / end
in het stof die verwarmt.

End vergheet / dat de voet die drucken kan / end de dieren des velts die
vertrappen konnen? Sy verhardet sich tegen hare jongen / als ofse hare niet en
waren: haren arbeydt is te vergeefs / om dat sy sonder brief i^. Want Godt
heeft haer van wisheyt ontbloot / end heeft haer des verstandts niets mede
gedeylt. Alst tijdt is / verheft sy haer inde hoochte: sy belaght het peert /
end sijn rijder.

Sult ghy het peert sterckte geven? kont ghy sijnen hals met donder bekleeden?
Sult ghy het beroeren / als eenen sprinck-haen? de pracht van sijn ghesnuyf is
eene verschrickinge. Het graeft inden gront / end het is vrolick in sijne
kracht: end treckt uyt / den geharnaschten te gemoete. Het belacht de breese /
end en wort niet ontsteldt / end en keert niet wederom van weghen het sweert.
Tegen hem totelt de pijl-koker; het vlammich yser der spiesse / end der lance:
Met schuddinghe end beroeringhe slockt het de aerde op / end en ghelooft niet
dat het is 't gheluydt der basuyne. In 't volle gheklanck der basuynen seydt
het Heaha: end rieckt de Krijch van verren / den donder der vorsten / end 't
ghejurch.

Vliecht de Sperwer door u verstant / end brendt sy hare vleugelen uyt nae het
su^den? Is It nae u bevel dat den Arent sich om hooghe verheft / end dat hy
sijnen nest inde hoochte maeckt: Hy wont end vernacht inde steen rotzse / op
de scherpte der s^een-rotze / end der vaster plaetse. van daer speurt hy de
spijse op ^sijne ooghen sien van verren a^. Oock suypen sijne jongen bloet end
waer verslaghene zijn daer is hy.

Siet nu / Behemoth / welcken ick ghemaeckt hebbe nevens u / hy eet hoy /
ghelijck even runt. Siet doch / sijne kracht is in sijne lendenen; end sijne
macht in den nave? sijns buyer. Als 't hem lust / sijnen steert is als even
Cedar: de senuwen zijn^r schaemte zijn doorvlochten. Sijne beenderen zijn als
vast koper: sijne gebeenten zijn als ysere hant-boomen. Hy is even hooft-stuck
der weghen Godts: die hem ghemaeckt heeft / k^n sijn sweert tot hem voegen. Om
dat de bergen hem voeder voortbrenghen / daerom spelen all de dieren des velis
aldaer. Onder schaduwachtige boomen leyt hy neder: in even schuyl plaetse des
riets / end des stijcks. De schaduwachtige boomen bedeckenhem / elck even met
sijne schaduwe: de beeck-wilghen omringen, hem, Siet / hy doet de riviere
gheweldt aen / end en verhaest sich niet hy bertrouwt / dat hy de Iordane in
sijnen mondt soude konnen intrecken. Soude men hem voor sijn ooghen konnen
vanghen? soude men hem met stricken den neuse doorboren konnen?

^ult ghy den Leviathan met den anghel trecken / often s^ne tonghe met eene
koorde / die ghy laet nedersincken? sult ghy hem eene angel in de neuse leggen:
of met even doorn sijne kake doorboren? sal hy aen u vele smeeckinghen waken?
sal hy sachtkens tot u spr^ken? sa^ by even verbont met u maken: sult ghy hem
aennemen tot eenen eeuwigen slave? sult ghy met hem spelen / ghe^^ck met even
vogelken: of su^t ghy hem binden voor uwe jonghe dochteren? sullen de
met-gesellen van hem even mael tijt bere^den: sullen sy hem deelen onder de
koop-lieden? Su^t ghy sijne hu^dt met haken vullen; of met even visschers
kranwel sijn hooft? Legt uwe hant op hem / gedenckt des strijdts / doet het
niet mere. Siet / sijne hope sal ferlen (...) sal hy oock niet voor sijn
ghesichte neder gheslaghen worden? riemant en is so koen / dat hy hem op wecken
soude; wie is dan hy / die sich voor mijn aenghesichte stellen soude? Wie heeft
m^ voor ghekomen / dat ick hem soude vergelden? wat onder den ^ensschen Hemel
is / is mijne. I^^t en sal sijne leden niet vers^^ijghen / nochte hei verhael
sijner ster^ten / nochte de bevallicheyt sijner ges^ altenisse, wie soude het
oppers^e sijnes ^^eets ontdecken (...) often wie soude met fijnen dobbelen
brerdel hem aenkemen? wie soude de deuren sijns aenghesic^^s open done? rontom
sijne tanden is verschrickinghe. Seer uytnemende zijn sijne stercke schilden;
elck even ghesloten als met eenen nauw-druckende zeghel.

De even is so na aenden anderen / dat de wint daer niet en kan tusschen komen.
Sy kleven aen malckanderen / sy vatten sich t'samen / datse fich niet en
scherden. Elck eene sijner niesinghen doet even licht schijnen: end sijne oogen
zijn als de oogen-leden des dageraets. With sijne mondt gaen fackelen / end
vyerighe voncken rakender uyt. With sijne neus-gaien komt roock voort / als uyt
eenen ziedenden pot / of ruymen ketel. Sijnen adem soude kolen done vlammen /
end even vlamme komt ur^ sijnen mondt voort. In sijnen hals herbergt de
sterckte: voor hem springht selve de droefheyt van vreuchden op De stucken
sijns vleeschs kleven to samen: elck even is vast in hem / het en wort niet
beweeght. Sijn heart is vast gelijck even sieentjke vast gelijck even deel des
ondersten meulen-steens. van sijn verheffen schromen del stercke: om sijner
doorbrekinghen will / ontsondigen sy hen.

Raeckt hem ymant met den sweerde / dat en sal niet bestaen; spiesse / schicht
/ noch pantzier. Hy acht het yser voor siroo / end het stael voor verrot hout.
De pijl en sal hem niet done vlieden: de slinghen-sieenen worden hem in
stoppelen verandert. De werp-steenen worden van hem gheachtet als stoppelen:
end hy belacht de drillinghe der lance. Onder hem zijn scherpe scherven: hy
spreyt sich op het punctachtighe / als op slijck. Hy doet de diepte zieden /
ghelijck eenen pot / hy stelt de Zee als, even Apotekers Kokerye. Achter hem
verlicht hy het padt: men soude den af-grondt voor grijsicheyt houden. Op der
aerden en is niet met hem te verghelijcken: die gemaeckt is / om sonder schrick
te wesen. Hy aensiet alles wat hooch is / hy is even koningh over all jonge
hooghmoedighe dieren.

The. 4, 5, and 6 chapters of the epistle of Paul to the Ephesians: wherein the
duty of Christians is largely handled.
I therefore beseech you, (even) I the prisoner in the Lord, that ye walk worthy
of the vocation wherewith ye are called: with all lowlines and meeknes, with
long suffering, forbearing one another in love: Endeavoring to keep the unity
of the Spirit by the bond of peace, There is one body, and one Spirit, even as
also ye are called unto one hope of your calling: one Lord, one faith, one
baptism, one God and father of all, who is above al, and through all, and in
you all.

But to every one of us is grace given, according to the measure of the gift of
Christ: Therefore he says, when he ascended up on high, he led captivity
captive, and gave gifts unto men. Now this, be ascended, what is it, but that
be also descended first into the lower parts of the earth? He that descended,
is the same also that ascended up far above all heavens, that he might fill
all things. And be gave some to be Apostles, and some for prophets, and some
to be Evangelists, and some for pastors and teachers: For the perfecting of
the Saints, for the work of the ministry, for the edifying of the body of
Christ; until we all come unto the unity of the faith and of the knowledge of
the son of God, unto a perfect man, unto the measure of the frature of the
fulness of Christ: That we henceforth be no more children, who like the flood
are tossed to and fro, and carried about with every wind of doctrine, by the
sleight of men, by the cunning craftines whereby they lie in wait to deceave:
But following the truth in love, may in all things grow up unto him, who is the
head, even Christ: From whom the whole body fitly joyned-togither and
compacted, by that which every joint supplyeth, according to the working of
every part in its measure, makes the increase of the body, to the edifying of
it self in love.

This I say therefore, and testify it in the Lord, that you henceforth walk
not like as the other gentiles walk in the vanity of their mind, darkened in
the understanding, being alienated from the life of God, through the ignorance
that is in them, because of the hardness of their hearts: who being past feeling,
have given themselves over unto lasciviousnes, to work all uncleannes with
greedines. But ye have not so learned Christ, if so be ye have but heard him,
and are taught by him, as the truth is in Jesus: To wit, that ye should put
off, concerning the former conversation, the old man, which is corrupt through
the lusts of deceitfulnes and that you should be renewed in the spirit of your
mind, and put on the new man, which after God is created in true
righteousness and holiness.

Wherefore put away lying and speak the truth every man with his neighbor: For
we are members one of another.

Be ye angry, and sin not; let not the sun go down upon your w^ath: neither
give place to the devil.

Let him that has stolen steal no more, but rather labor, working with his
hands the thing which is good, that he may have to distribute to him that has
need.

Let no filthy communication proceed out of your mouth: but if there be any
good communication to profitable edification, that it may give grace to them
that bear it.

And grieve not the holy Spirit of God, by whom ye are sealed unto the day of
redemption.

Let all bitterness, and wrath, and anger, and clamor, and evil speaking, be
put away from you, withal malice.

But be ye kind one to another, merciful, forgiveing one another, even as also
God in Christ has forgiven you.

Be ye therefore followers of God, as dear children: and walk in love, even
as Christ also has loved us, and has given himself up for us, for an
offerring and a sacrifice to God, for a sweet smelling savor.

But fornication, and al uncleannes, or covetousnes, let it not be once named
among you, as it becomes Saints: neither filthynes, nor foolish talking, or
jesting, which are not comely, but rather giving of thanks. For this you know,
that no whoremonger, or unclean (person), or covetous (man) Who is an Idolater,
has inheritance in the kingdom of Christ and of God.

That no man deceave you with vain words: for because of these things comes
the wrath of God upon the children of disobedience. Be not ye therefore
partakers with them. For ye were sometimes darkness, but now are ye light in
the Lord: walk as children of light: For the fruit of the Spirit is in all
goodness, and righteousness, and truth. Proveing what is acceptable unto the Lord.

And have no fellowship with the unfruitful works of darkness: but much rather
also reprove them. For it is even shameful to speak of those things which are
don of them in secret. But al these things, being reproved of the light are
made manifest. For whatsoever does make manifest, is light. Therefore he says,
Awake thou that sleep, and arise from the dead, and Christ shall give thee
light,

See then thae ye walk circumspectly, not as fools but as wise, redeeming the
time, because the days are evil. wherefore be ye not without understanding,
but understand what the will of the Lord is. And be not drunk with wine,
wherein is excess, but be filled with the Spirit: Speaking among your selves
with psalms; and hymns, and spiritual songs, singing, and making melody to
the Lord in your heart: giving thanks always for all things to God and the
father, in the name of our Lord Jesus Christ: being subject one to another in
the fear of God.

Ye wives be subject to your own husbands, as unto the Lord: For the husband
is the head of the wife, even as Christ is the head of the church; and he is
the savior of the body. Therefore as the Church is subject unto Christ, so also
(^e^) the wives (be) to th ir own husbands in every thing Ye husbands love
your own w^ves, even as Christ also has loved the Church, and has given up
himself for her: that he might sanctify it, having cleansed her with the
washing o^ wa^er by the word: toa^ he might present it to himself gloriou^^ a
church which has no spot or wrinckle, or any such thing, but that she should
be ho^y and v^^t proveable. So are men bound to love their own wives, as their
own bodies. He that loves his own wife, loves himself. For no man ha h yet
ever bated his own flesh, but he nourishe^h and cherrisheth it, even as also
the Lord the church. For we are members of his body, of his flesh and of his
bones. Therefore shall a man leave his father and mother and shall cleave to h s
Wi^e: and they two shall be one flesh. This mystery is great: but I speak this,
having respect unto Christ, and unto the church. Therefore also let every one of
you in particular so love his wife as himself: and the wife see that she
reverence her husband.

Ye children be obedient to your parents in the Lord: for that is right. Honor
thy father and mother (which is the first commandment with a promise) that it
may go well with thee, and that thou may live long upon the earth. And ye
fathers, provoke not your children to wrath: but bring them up in the nurture
and admonition of the Lord.

Ye servants be obedient unto your Masters according to the flesh, with fear
and trembling, in singlenes of your heart, as unto Christ: not according to
eye-service, as men pleasers, but as servants of Christ, doing the will of God
from the heart; with good will doing service to the Lord and not to men:
knowing that whatsoever good thing any man does, the same shall he receave of
the Lord, whither he be bond or free. And ye Masters, do the same things to
them, forbearing threatening: as knowing that also your Master is in heaven,
and that no respect of persons is with him.

Furthermore, my brethren, be strong in the Lord, and in the power of his
might. Put on the whole armor of God, that you may stand against the crafty
wiles of the devil. For we wrestle not against flesh and blood, but against
principalities, against powers, against the rulers of the world, of the darkness
of this world, against Spiritual wickednesses in the air. Therefore take on
the whole armor of God, that you may be able to withstand in the evil day, and
having finished all to abide standing. Stand therefore, having your loins girt
about with truth, and having put on the breast plate of righteousness: and
having your feet shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace. Above all
having taken on the shield of faith, wherewith ye shall be able to quench all
the fiery darts of the wicked: And take the helmet of salvation, and the sword
of the Spirit, which is the word of God: praying always with all prayer and
supplication in the Spirit, and watching thereunto with all perseverance, and
supplication for all Saints. And for me, that Speech may be given to me in the
opening of my mouth with boldness, to make known the mystery of the gospel
for which I am an ambassador in a chain, that in the same I may speak boldly
as I ought to speak.

And that ye also may know mine affairs, and what I do, Tychicus the beloved
brother, and faithful minister in the Lord shall make known to you all things:
whom I have sent unto you for the same purpose, that you may know our affairs,
and that he may comfort your hearts,

Peace be to the brethren, and love with faith, from God the father, and the
Lord Jesus Christ. Grace be withal them, that lover our Lord Jesus Christ in
incorruption, Amen.

De 4, 5, en 6 capittelen des Sendt-briefs Pauli aen den Ephesenen: waerin de
plicht der Christenen in it breet verhandelt wordt.
SO bid ick u dan / ick de gevangen in den Here / dat ghy wandelt
weerdighlick der roepinge / met welcke ghy gheroepen zijt: Met all
ootmoedigheyt end sachtmoedigheyt / met lanckmoedigheydt / verdragende

door den bant des vredes. Even lichaem is het / en^ eenen geest ghelij^kerwijs
ghy oock geroepen zijt tot eene hope uwer beroepinghe: even Here / even gheloove
/ eenen doop / even Godt end Dader van all / die daer is boven all / end
door all / end in u ^lle.

Maer elck even van ons is de genade ghegeven / na de ^ate der gave Christi
Daerom feght hy / Als hy opghevaren is in de hooghte / heeft hy de
gevanckenisse gevanghen ghenomen / end heeft den menschen gaven gegeven. Nu
dit / hy is opgevaren / wat is 'r / dan dat hy cock eerst is nederghedaelt in
de nedersie deelen der aerde? Die nedergedaelt is / is de felve oock die
opghevaren is verre boven all de Hemolen / op dat hy all dinghen vervullen
soude. Er de de selve heeft gegeven sommige tot Apostelen / end sommige tot
Propheeten / end sommighe tot Evangelisten / end sommighe tot Herders end
Leeraers: Tot de volmakinghe der Heylighen / tot het werck der bedieninge / tot
opbouwinge des Lichaems Christi; tot dat wy all sullen komen tot de eenigherdt
des gheloofs end der kennisse des Soons Godts / tot eenen ^elkomenen man / tot
de mate der groote der volheyt Christi* op dat wy niet mere kinderen en souden
zijn / die als de v^eedt beweeght end omghevoert worden met all wini der
^eere / doer de bedrieghetie der menschen / door archlis^igheyt om lis^elick
tot dwalinghe ^e brengen: Magd de wacrhe^dt betr^chtende in liefde / alles^ns
souden op wassen in hem die het hooft is / namelijck Chris^us: uyt welcken het

ghelijck deel in sijne mate / den wasoom des Lichaems maeckt / tot sijns selfs
ophouwinghe in de Liefde.

I^k seg^he dan dit / end betuyghe het in den Here dat ghy niet mere en

verdu^ stert in het verstant / vervremt zijnde van het leven God^s / door de

ontuch^igh^yt / om all onreynighe dt gierighlick te bedrijven. Doch gh^ en

Wort toornich / end en fondight niet: de Son en ^ae niet onder over uwe

The ghestoren heeft / en stele niet mere / maer arbeyde liever / werckende dat

Gheen buyle re^en en gae uyt uwen mondt: maer so daer eenighe goede reden is

End en bedroeft den Heyligen Geest Goot niet / door welcken ghy verseghelt
zijt tot den va^h der veriossenghe.

All bitterhert / end toorniche^t / end gramschap / end gheroep / end
lasteringhe zy van u geweert / met all booshegt.

Maer zijt tegen malkanderen goedertieren / barmhertigh / verghevende
malkanderen / ghelijckerwijs oock God in Christo u lieden vergheven heeft.

Zijt dan na-volgers Godts / als gheliefde kinderen: end wandelt in de liefde
/ ghelijckerwijs oock Christus ons lief gehadt heeft / end hem selven voor ons
heeft overghegeven tot even offerhande end even slacht offer Good / tot eenen

Maer hoererre / end all ondeynicheyt / often giericheyt / en laet oock onder
u niet ghenaemt worden / ghelijckerwijs het den heyligen betaemt: noch
oneerbaerheyt / noch sot-geklap often geckerye / welcke niet en betamen; maer
veel mere danck-segginge. Want dit weet ghy, dat gheen hoereerder / often
onreyne / often gierigaert / die even af-goden dienaer is / erffenisse en heeft
in het Coninckrijcke Christi end Godts.

Dat u niemandt en ver^e^de met ydele woorden: want om dese dinghen komt de
soorne Gods ober de kinderen der ongehoorsaemheyt. So en zijt dan hare mede
ghenooten niet. want ghy waert eertijts duysternisse / maer nu zijt ghy licht
in den Here; wandelt als kinderen das lichts: want de vrucht des Geefts is in
all goedigheyt / end rechtveerdigheyt / end waerheyt. Beproebende wat den
Here well behagelijck zy.

End en hebt geen gemeynschap met de onvruchtbare wercken der duysternisse /
maer bestraftse oock veel eer. Want het gene heymelijck van haer geschiet / is
schandelijck oock te seggen. Maer all defe dinghen / van het licht bestraft
sijnde / worden openbaer want all dat openbaer maeckt / is licht. Daerom seght
hy / Ontwaeckt ghy die slaept / end staet opuyt den dooden / end Christus sal
over u lichten.

Siet dan hoe ghy voorsichtelijck wandelt / niet als onwijse / maer als wijfe
den tijt uytcoopende / dewijle de dagen boos zijn Daerom enzijt niet
onverstandigh / maer vers^aet welcke de will des Heeren zy. End en wort niet
droncken in wijn / waer in overdaet is / maer wort vervult met den Geest:
sprekende onder malkanderen met Psalmen / end lof-sanghen / end Gheestelijcke
liedekens singhende / end psalmende den Here in uw' heart: danckende all
tijdt over all dingen Godt end den Dader / inden name onses Heeren Jesus
Christi. Malkanderen onderdanigh zijnde in de vreese Gods.

Ghy brouwen weest uwe eyghene mannen onderdanigh / ghelijck den Here: want de
Man is het hooft des wijfs / gelijck oock Christus het hooft der Geme^nte is:
end hy is de behouder des Lichaenis.

Daerom ^elijck de Gemeynte Christo onderdanigh is / also ooel de vrouwen hare
e^gene mann^n in alles. Ghy mannen hebt uwe eyghene Drouwen Lief / gelijck oo k

di^^ghelijcke / maer dat sy soude Heyli^h sijn end on^^^ dispelijck. Also zijn
de mannen schu digh hare ^^ghene brouwen ^^ef te hebben / ghe^^ck haere eygh^ne
^^chamen. Die fijne e^^ here Drouwe lief heeft die heeft hem ^r^v^n lief. Wan^
niemandi en heeft oyt sijn erghen vleesch gehaet / ma^r hy vo^^ het / end
onderhout het / gelijckerwijs oock de Here de Geme nie: Want wy zijn leden
zijns Lichaems / van sijnen vleesche / end van sijne beenen. Daerom sal even
mensche sijneu Dader end Moeder ver alen / end sal sijn Wijf aenhanghen: end
sy twee sullen tot even bleesch wesen. Dese verborghentheyt is groot: does ick
segghe dit siende op Christum / end op den Ge^^e nie. So dan oock ghy lied^n
elck in 't bysonder / even gegelijck hebbe sijn eygen Drouwe also lief als hem
selven: end de Drouwe sie dat sy den man breese.

Ghy kinderen zijt uwen ouderen gehoorsaem in den Here: want dat is recht.
Eert uwen Vader / end Moeder / (het welck het eerste gebodt is met even
belofte) op dat het u well gae / end dat ghy langhe leeft op de aerde. End gh^
Daders en verweckt uwe kinderen niet tot toorne / maer voedtse op in de
leeringhe end vermaninghe des Heeren.

G^^ dienst-knechten zijt gehoorsaem uwen Heeren na den vleesche / met vrese
end beven / in eenvoudighe^dt uwes herten / ghelijck als Christo: niet not
ooghen-dienst / als menschen behagers / maer als dienst-knechten Christi /
doende den will Godis van herten; dienende met goetwilligheydt den Here /
end niet den menschen: we tend dat so wat goet even regelijck gedaen sal
hebben / hy dat selve van den Here sal ontfangen; het zydienst-knecht / 't z^

wetet dat oock uw' selfs Here in de Hemelen is / end dat geen aenneminghe des

Doorders / mijne broeders / wordet krachtigh in den Here / end in de
sterckte zijner macht. Doet aen de gheheele wapen-rustinge Godts / op dat ghy
konnet staen tegen de listighe omle^dinghen des Duyvels. Want wy en hebben den
strijt niet tegen vleesch end bloet / maer tegen de overheden / teghen de
