alles verricht hebbende / staende blijven. Staet dan / uwe lenden omgegordt
hebbende met de waerheyt / end aengedaen hebbende de borst-wapen der
gerechticheyt: end de voeten geschoeyt hebbende met bereydtheyt des
Evangeliums des vredes. Boven al aenghenomen hebbende de schildt des gheloofs /
met welcken ghy all de vyerighe pijlen des boosen sult konnen uyt-blusschen:
End neemt den helm der Salicheydt / end het sweerdt des Geesis / het welck is
Godts woordt: Met all biddinge end smeeckinge / biddende tot aller tijdt in
den Gheest / end tot het selve wakende met all gheduericheydt / end
smeeckinge voor all de Herlighe: End voor my / op dat my het woordt ghegheven
word in de openinghe mijns mondts met vrymoedigheydt / om de verborghentheydt
des Evangeliums bekent te maken / waer over ick even ghesante ben in even keten /
op dat ick in it selve vrymoedelijck match spreken / ghelijck my betaemt te
spreken.

End op dat oock ghy mooght weten het ghene my aengaet / end wat ick do /
dat alles sal u Tychicus de geliefde broeder end ghes^ouwe Dienaer in den
Here bekent maken: den welcken ick tot dien selven eynde tot u ghesonden hebbe
/ op dat ghy onse saken soude tweten / end hy uwe herten soude vertroosten

Vrede zy den broederen / end liefde met gheloove / van Godt den Dader / end
den Here Jesus Christo.

De ghenade zy met all de ghene / die onsen Here Iesum Christum lief hebben
in onverderflijckheydt. Amen.

Psalm. 91
HE that dwells in the hideing-place of the most high, he shall rest in the
shadow of the Almighty.

I will say to the Lord; My refuge and my fortress my God in whom I trust.

For he shall rid thee from the snare of the fowler: from the grievous
destructive pestilence.

He shall cover thee with his feathers, and under his wings shall thou trust:
his truth is a shield and buckler.

Thou shall not be afraid for the terror of the night: for the arrow that
flies by day, for the pestilence that walks in darkness: for the destruction
that wastes at noonday.

A thousand shall fall at thy side, and ten thousand at thy r^ght hand: it shall
not come nigh thee. On^y with thine eyes shall thou behold it* and thou shall
see the reward of the wicked.

For thou, oh Lord, art my refuge, thou have made the most high thine
habitation there shall none evil befall thee, neither shall any plague come
nigh thy tent. For he shall give his Angels charge of thee, that they keep
thee in all thy wajes. They shall bear thee upon their hands, that thou dash
thy foot against no stone.

Thou shall tread upon the fierce lion and the adder, thou shall trample under
feet the young lion and the dragon.

Because he loves me much (says God) therefore will I deliver him: I will set
him on high, for he knows my name. He shall call upon me, and I will hear
him: I will be with him in trouble, I will draw him cut, and will honor him.
I will satisfy him with length of days, and will cause him to see my salvation.

Psalm. 91.
DIe in de schuyl-plaetse des Alderhooghsten is geseten / die sal vernachten in
de schaduwe des Almachtighen.

Ick fall tot den Here segghen; Mijne toevlucht end mijn burcht: mijn Godt op
welcke ick vertrouwe.

Want hy sal u redden van den strick des voghel-vangers: van de seer
verderflicke pesiilentie.

Hy sal u decken met sijne blercken / end onder sijne vleugelen sult ghy
betrouwen: sijne waerheydt is even rondasse end beukelaer.

Ghy en sult niet vreesen voor den schrick des nachts: voor den pijl die des
daechs vliecht: voor de pestilentie die in de donckerheyt wandelt: voor het
verderf dat op den middach verwoestet.

Aen uwe zijde sullender duysent vallen / end tien duysent aen uwe rechter
hant tot u en sal 't niet genaken. Allcenlijck sult ghy 't met uwe oogen
aenschouwen end ghy sult de vergeldinge der godtloosen sien.

Want ghy / Here / zijt mijne toevlucht den Alderhoochsten hebt ghy ghestelt
tot u vertreck / ^en sal gheen quaet wedervaren / noch geen plage sal uwe tente
naderen. Want hy sal sijne Engelen van u bevelen / datse u bewaeren in all uwe
wegen. Sy sullen u op de handen dragen / op dat ghy uwen voet aen geenen steen
en stootet.

Op den fellen leeuw end d'adder sult ghy treden / ghy sult den jongen Leeuw /
end de drake vertreden.

Dewijle h^ my seer bemint / (spreeckt Godt) so sal ick hem uythelpen: ick sal
hem op eene hoochte stellen / want hy kent mijnen name. Hy sal my aenroepen /
end ick sal hem verhooren: in de benaeuwtherdt sal ick by hem zijn / ick
salder hem uyttrecken / end sal hem vereerlicken. Ick sal hem met lanckheydt
der dagen verfadighen / end sal hem mijn Saligheydt done sien.

Certain moral sayings, and familiar (or proverbiall) speeches, very pleasant
to the mind, and profitable for the exercise of the tongue.
Eenige stichtelijcke spreucken, en gemeene (of proverbiale) spreeck-woorden,
den Geest seer vermaeckelijck, en voordelijk tot d'oeffeninge der sprake.
1 Of the fear of God. Van de vrese des Heeren.
Honor and serve God.

Eert en dient Godt.

Follow piety.

Behertichd de Godsaligheydt.

The fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom.

De vreese des Heeren is 't beginn' der wijsheyt.

In all that thou say or do, remember that God hears and sees it.

In all' het geen ghy seght of doet / denckt dat God het hoort en siet.

God punishes evil and rewards good.

Godt straft het quade / end beloont het goede.

Godliness is the foundation of all virtue

Godt vruchticheyt is de grondt van all deuchden.

2 Of duty to parents and superiors. Van 't plicht aen ouders en overheden.
LOve thy parents.

Hebt uwe ouders lief.

Strive not with thy parents, although thou have right in what thou say.

En twist niet met uw' ouders / al hebt ghy schoon ghelijck in 't gene ghy
seght.

Like as thou dealest with thy parents, so shall thy children deal with thee.

Gelijck ghy met uw' ouders handelt / so sullen uw' kinderen met u handelen.

Yield some what to your elder.

Geeft uwe meerder wat toe.

Respect thy friends.

Houdt uwe vrunden in waerde.

Honor them to whom honor is due,

Gert die gheene die eere toe komt.

Fear thy master.

Ontsiet uwe meester.

Reverence an aged person.

Zijt eerbiedigh tegen even oud bejaarde.

Obey the laws and ordinances.

Onderhout de keuren en ordonantien.

Esteem thy sell little among great ones.

By den grooten hout u kleyn.

3 of duty to a man's self. Van d' plicht aen eens selven.
PReserve thy substance.

Bewaerd uwe goed.

Look to preserve honor and grace.

Siet eer en schaamt te behouden.

Preserve thy good name.

Bewaard uwe goeden naam.

Know thy self.

Kendt u selven.

Be like thy self.

Zijt u selfs ghelijck.

If a man cut off his nose, he marreth his face.

Snijt men sijn neus af / so schent hy sijn aengesicht.

Every man for himself, and God for us all.

Elck voor hem selven / en Godt voor ons allen.

Who brings water to his neighbors house, when his own is on fire?

Wie brenght water aen sijn buer man's huys / als sijn eyghen brandt?

Every one will have the butter on his own cake.

Elck will de boter on sijn koeck hebben.

4 of duty to neighbors. Van de plicht tot d'even-naesten.
WHat thou would not have don to thee, that do not to another

't Geen ghy niet en wilt dat u geschiede / 't selve doet dan oock even ander
niet.

With such measure as thou shall have measured to an other shall be measured to
thee again.

Met sulcke mate als ghy jemant sult ghemeeten hebben / sal u weder toe
gemeeten worden.

5 of repentance. Van bekeeringe.
Have thou erred? then change thy counsel.

Hebt ghy gedwaelt, so verandert van raet.

Hard jogs (shakings) teach well.

Hard schocken leeren well.

He that strayeth and quickly returns, is thereby taught better.

Wie dwaelt / en haestigh weder keert /

Die worter beter door geleert.

By falling men learn to go sure.

Met vallen leertmen seker gaen.

A burnt child dreads the fire.

Even verbrant kindt vreest het vier.

6 of virtue. Vande deucht.
GLory is the shadow of virtue.

Eere is de schaduwe des deuchds.

Honest men hate evil doing, through love to virtue.

De vrome haten 't quaad done / door liefde totte deuchd.

7 Education of children Opvoedinghe van kinderen.
THe twig must be bent while it is render.

Terwijle het rijs swack is moetmen het buygen.

He that loves his child well, will chastise him.

Die well bemint: castijt zijn kint.

'T is ill leading old dogs in a string.

'T is quaet oude honden aen banden te leggen.

Custom is a second nature.

Gewoonte is de tweede nature.

Correction brings fruit.

Tucht baert vrucht.

What one in youth well learn can,

That hangs him all his life time on.

Wat heeft geleert de jonger man /

Dat hangt hem al sijn leven an.

What is bred in the bone will not out of the f^esh.

Dat int gebeente gegroeyt is / will uyt het vleesch niet

Teach a child in the way he should go: and when he is old, he will not depart
from it. Pro. 22.6.

Leert den iongen de eerste beginselen na den eysch sijns weghs: als hy oock
oudt sal geworden zijn / en sal hy daer van niet af wijcken.

8 Of pride and humility. Van hoovardye, en nedericheyt.
BE not high minded.

En zijt niet hoogh-dragende.

Despise not, nor reject thy inferior.

En veracht noch verstoot uw' minder niet.

The higher the mountain the lower the vale*

The greater the tree, the harder the fall.

Hoe hooger bergh / hoe laeger dal:

Hoe grooter boom / hoe swaerder val.

Do thou fear the lightening? then duck.

Dreesje voor den blic^em? so duyckt.

He that abides low, cannot fall hard.

Die laegh blijft kan niet hard vallen.

Lowly set, and richly warm.

Laegh geseten en rijckelijcken warm.

will thou not be shot, then stoop down.

Wilje niet geschoten worden / so huyck neder.

A man forgotten, has the best.

Even vergeten man / isser best aen.

God resists the proud, but gives grace to the humble. Iam. 4 6.

Godt wederstaet de hoevaerdige / maer de nederighe gheeft hy genade.

9 Of covetousnes and liberality. Van giericheyt en mildicheyt.
A Miser does no good, but when he dies.

Even gierigaerd doet niet goeds / dan als hy sterft.

Dear s^a-men often times stay on shore.

Diere Schippers veel tijts aen lant blijven.

Great fishes tear the net.

Groote visschen scheuren 't net.

Men must not swallow such great brocks as to choke them.

Men moet so groote brocken niet inswelghen / datmer aen wurght.

Hired horses mak-short miles.

Gehuerde peerden maken korte mijlen.

It Is good bidding guests woere the provision cost nothing.

Daer 't vry ghelagh is / is it goed gasten noden.

It Is easy to make a good fire of an others turf.

It Is licht goed vyer maken van even anders turf.

It 's good cutting large girths of an other man's leather.

'T is goet breed riemen snijden uyt even ander man's leer.

It Is good to keep feast in an others hall.

It Is goed feast houden op even anders zael.

It Is good dancing on an other man's floor.

It Is goed danssen op even ander man's vloer.

He that hunteth two hares at once gets neither.

Die twee Haesen gelijck jaeght / krijght geen van beyden.

Fathom much, but ga^her little.

Deel om vamen / weynigh versamen,

Great pears may hurt.

Groote peeren konnen deeren.

10 of hatred and envy. Van haet en nyt.
SPite gapes wide.

Spijt gaept wijt.

when love turns into hatred, then is it unmeasurable.

Als liefde keert in haet:

Dan gaetse buyten maet.

Envy cries of spite where honor rides.

Nijt krijt van spijt / waer eere rijt.

It grieveth one dog, that the other goes into the kitchen.

'T is den eenen hont leet / dat d'ander in de keucken gaet.

Who so prospers well, is envyed.

Wie well gedht / die wort benijt.

After honor and dignity, follows envy and hatred.

Naer eer en staet; volght nijt en haet.

Wrath is cruel and anger is outrageous but who is able to stand against envy?
Pro. 27.4.

Grimmicheyt / end overloopinge van toorn is wreetheyt: maer wie fall voor
nijdicheyt bestaen?

11 of wisdom and knowledge. Van wysheyt en wetenschap.
MEn must respect wisdom above strength.

Men moet de wijsheyt boven de sterckte aensien.

Wealth is uncertain and fading: but knowledge abides alwajes.

Rijckdem is onseeker en verganckelijck / maer de wetenschap blijft altijt.

Be not ashamed to learn.

En schaamt u niet te leeren.

Remember what thou have read.

Onthout dat ghy gelesen hebt.

Fools despise wisdom and learning.

De sotten verachten wijsheydt end leeringe.

There is nothing more excelent than knowledge.

Daer is niet treffelijcker als wetenschap.

12 Of patience and anger. Van lydtsaemheydt en toornicheydt.
IN prosperity think of adversity:

In voorspoet denckt op tegenspoet.

Bear that which thou suffer by thine own fault.

Verdraeght het gene ghy door u eygen schult lijdt.

Men go not laughing to heaven.

Men komt niet lachende inden Hemel.

Be not angry without cause.

En wild niet toornich wesen sonder oorsaak.

Anger is a short madness, or a noise tha^ ^ast^th not long,

Gramschap is even korte dullicheydt / of even raserie die niet lang duurt.

A man of little understanding is soon angry.

Even mensche van kleyn verstandt is haeft verstoort,

A little po^ is soon hot.

Even kleyne Pot were haeft heet.

To a little oven there needs little fire.

Tot even kleynen oven isser weynich vyers van noode

Many think it to be great honor to suffer nothing (patiently): but sound
doctrine teaches clearly, that there is no greater magnanimity than to be able
to suffer injury with patience.

Deel meynen groote eer te zijn niet te verdragen: maer de gesonde leere wijst
klaerlijck uyt / datter gheen meerder grootmoedigheyt en is / als onghelijck
met ghedult te konnen lijden.

13 Of temperance and mediocrity. Van maticheyt en middelmaer.
BE neither prodigal nor covetous.

En weest niet verquistich noch gierich.

He shund the rain and fell into the ditch.

Hy schoude de regen en diel inde sloot.

Toe pitcher goes so long to the water, till at last it breaks.

De kruyck gaet so lang te water / tot datse eens breeckt.

He is a fool who suffers much pain for an hare: and yet kills an horse worth
many pounds.

Hy is even dwaes / die om even haes / veel smerten lijt:

En noch even peert veel ponden weert / den hals af tijl.

High trees give more shadow than fruit.

Hooghe boomen geven mere schaduwe als vruchten.

He that the candle too deep does cut,

Blows lightly all her luster out.

Wie de keers te diepe snijt /

Blust well licht haere luyster uyt.

Men must sheare the sheep, according as they have wool,

Men moet de schapen scheeren na zy wol hebben.

Cut the herb so that it may continue growing.

If thou wring'st too hard, the nose must bleed.

Snijt so het kruyt dat het match blijven groejen.

Snuyt ghy te heart so moet de neuse bloeyen.

When a man is satisfied, then a bony comb rellisheth not.

Wanneer men is versaet.

Dan smaeckt geen honig raet.

Drunckennes is sin, loss, and shame.

Dronkenschap is sonde / schade / en schande.

Enough, is as good as a fealt.

Genoech is even so goed als even Feast.

Too much of one thing, is good for nothing.

Te veel van eenen dingh is niewers nut toe.

They that drink wine without relish, commit a great error.

Die wijn drincken sonder smaeck:

Done even onbesuijsde saeck.

Who so drincks without thirst,

and eats without hunger,

He dies the younger.

Wie drinckt sonderdorst /

En eet sonder honger /

Die sterft te jonger.

14 Of good and bad Company. Van goed en quaedt gheselschap.
COnverse with the good.

Gaet met de vrome om.

Convers with wise folks.

Derkeert met wijse luyden.

Esteem much of honest people.

Hout veel van vrome luyden.

An evil man is the worst beast.

Even quaet mensch is 't alderslimste beeft

It is good, to have dealing with good men.

Met den goeden is 't goet done.

Beware of bad company.

Wacht u voor quade gheselschap.

One rotten apple in the basket, spoileth also the sound fruit.

Even rotten appel in de mande.

Maeckt oock het gave fruit te schande.

If thou touchest pitch thou shall be defiled.

Handelt ghy peck: ghy krijght even vleck.

Among wolves and owls, men learn to howl.

By wolven en uylen: daer leertmen huylen.

One scabbed sheep spoils the whole flock.

Even schurft schaep bederft de heel kudde.

One fool makes many.

Eenen dwase maeckter veul.

He that dwells with cripples, learneth to limpe.

Die by de kreupelen wont / leert hincken.

He that lies with dogs gets fleas.

Die met honden gaet te bed /

Deelt van haer vloeyen met.

Foul ground spoils the cables.

Duyle gronden bederven de kabels.

Woo so hunteth with cats,

Catches naught save rats.

Die jaeght met katten /

En vanght maer ratten.

It Is ill working with bad tools.

Met quaed tuyg is it quaet wercken.

He that mingleth himself among draffe, is eaten of the Swines.

Wie sich onder de draf mengt / werdt van de Swijnen gegeten.

Better alone, than with bad company.

Beeter alleen als qualijck verselt.

He that dwells near a mill, is made dusty with the meal.

Die ontrent even molen wont / bestuyft van het mee^.

He that walks with wise men shall be wise: but a Companion of fools shall be
destroyed. Pro. 13.20.

Die met de wijse om gaet / sal wijs worden: maer die de sotter met geselle is
/ sal verbroken worden.

15 Of Courtesy, and kindness. Van beleeftheyt en vriendelyckheyt.
SAlute willingly.

Groet gaerne.

Be not hard to those that are under you.

Dalt uwe minder niet hard.

Be friendly in speec^.

Zijt vriendelijck in it spreken.

As thou salutest another, so shall thou again be saluted.

Gelijck ghy even ander sult groeten / so sult ghy weder gegroetet worden.

Do good to the good.

Doet den bromen goet.

Honor them which have do thee good.

Eertse die u goed ghedaen hebben.

Do good even to thine enemies,

Doet oock uw' vyanden goed.

Recompense a good turn.

Door even weldaet doet vergeldingh^.

Men lock up no bread from friends.

Men sluyt geen broot voor de vrienden.

16 Of the tongue, and the good or evil use thereof. Van de tonghe, en het
goed of quaad gebruyck der selve.
BEfore thou speak, meditate well what thou will say.

Eer ghy spreeckt / versint well wat ghy seggen wilt,

Hear much, but speak little.

Hoord veel / maer spreeckt weynich,

Many things befall him that speaks much.

Die veel kalt / die veel ontvalt.

To the wise there is soon enough spoken.

Den verstandigen is it haest genoech geseyt.

A word to the wise is enough.

Aen den verstandigen is even word ghenoech.

Evil words corrupt good manners.

Boose reden / bederven goede seden.

Agreement in speech, or offitiousnes makes friends; but speaking the truth
causes ill will or hatred.

Geseghelijckheyt of gediensticheyt maackt vrienden / maer waerheydt te spreken
veroorsaackt onminne of haat.

He that has gall in his mouth can not spit honey.

Die gal heeft in de mondt en kan gheen honigh spouwen.

Little said is soon amended.

Weynigh geseyt is haeft verbeetert.

He that would alwajes live at rest,

Must bear, and see, and say the best.

Die sijn tijt in rust will leven /

Moet hooren en sien / en't best spreken.

Silence and thought can hurt no body.

Swijghen en dencken / kan niemant kreucken.

Many flags, little butter,

Deel vlaggen / luttel boters.

They are empty vessels which make the greatest sound,

't Zijn ledighe vaten / die meest bommen,

Still waters have deep bottomes.

Stille waters / hebben diepen gronden.

Full vessels sound not.

Volle vaten bommen niet.

A man that speaks not, and a dog that barks not, must at all times be most
narrowly looked to.

Even mensch die niet en spreeckt /

Even hont die niet en bast /

Daer dient tot aller tijt /

Ten nausten op gepast.

Fools will first give their judgment.

Dwasen willen eerst oordeelen.

The cripple will be first in the dance.

Den krepel will eerst aen den dans.

The worse carpenter, the more chips.

Hoe slimmer timmerman / hoe meerder spaenders.

The worse wheel, the more it crakes.

Hoe slimmer wiel / hoe mere het kraeckt.

One penny in the spare-pot makes more noise, than when it is full.

Even penningh in den spaerpot maeckt mere geraes / dan als sy vol is.

An empty fat sounds most.

Even ydel vat bomt aldermeest.

Great boast; little roast.

Groot roemen; weynich gebraedt.

Great talkers no great doers.

Groot sprekers sijn geen groot-daeders.

The goose blows indeed, but biteth not.

De gans blaest well / maer en bijt niet.

They do not all bite, that show their teeth.

Sy en byten niet al / die haer tanden laeten sien.

A cat that meweth much, catches but few mice.

Even kat die veel maeuwt / vangt weynig muysen.

Threateners fight not.

Dreygers en vechten niet.

Threats are the weapons of the threatened.

Het dreygen is der gedreygden geweer.

When thieves fall out true men come to their goods,

Wanneer dieven kijven / bekomen vrome lieden hare goederen.

Cowardly dogs bark much.

Blood honden bassen veel.

Scabbed sheep bleat most.

Schurfde Schapen bleeten meest.

Still sowes eat up all the draffe.

Stille seugen eeten al de draff op.

A threatened man, lives seven years.

Even ghedreygt man leeft seven jaeren.

Long of tongue, short of hand.

Langhe tonghe kort van handt.

Dissembling cats take the flesh out of the pot.

De luypende katten halen het vlees uyt de pot.

The more love the less speech.

Hoe meerder liefde hoe minder spraeck.

Full ears of corn hang lowest.

De volle koren-ayren hangen laegst.

Every bird sings according as he is beacked,

Elcke vogelke singt so het gebeckt is.

Men see whether the Hog be measeld by his tongue.

Men siet aen de tongue often vercken gortich is.

Foul mouths foul bottomes,

Duyle monden vuyle gronden.

The vessel gives ou^ such as is in it.

Het vat geeft uyt so het in heeft.

Men know trees by the fruit, and a wanton heart by its sport.

Men kent de boomen aen de vruchten /

Even weeldigh hertje by de kluchten.

Unclean birds seldom crow good weather.

Onreyne vogels kraeyen seldom goet weder.

A cuckoo cries out his own name.

Even Koeckoeck roept sijn eygen naem uyt.

17 Of backbiting. Van achter-klap.
SPeak none evil of any one behind his back.

En spreeckt geen quaad van jemandt achter sijn rugge.

He must have a great deal of fromity that will stop every ones mouth.

Hy moet veel brijs hebben die elck den mondt sal stoppen.

He must rise betimes who will please every body.

Hy moet vroegh op staen die alleman believen will.

Its bad straightening all crooked timber.

It Is quaet all krom houten rechten.

Men can hardly take care of all.

Men kant qualijck al besorgen.

It Is bad hanging yarne before all holes.

Voor all gaten is it quaet garen hangen.

With holding ones tongue all things may be overcome; but not with wrangling.

Men kan all dingh doot swijgen / niet doet kijven.

He is truly a skillful man who can make all well.

It Is voorwaer even kunstigh man.

Die het al well maken kan.

18 Of Corruption, and nature, Van verdorventheyt, end aerdt.
MEn will be alwajes thwart in the way.

Altijt wilmen dwars in de weghen.

None among men is wise at all times.

Niemant onder de menschen is t'aller uren wijs.

An old hunter delights to hear of hunting.

Even oudt jager hoort geerne van de weyery.

It has soon rayned enough in a wet pool.

In even natten poel is haest genoegh geregent.

The hoarie frost comes quickly on old ice.

Het tijpt haest op even oudt is.

A wolf catches at the sheep, when he is a dying,

Even wolf hapt noch na 't schaep / als hem de Ac^e uyt gaat.

He is not yet wholly free, that draws a piece of his bands after him.

Hy is niet geheel vry die noch even stuck van sijn banden nae-sleept.

Not only the leaf but the root must be plucked up of weeds.

Van't onkruyt dient niet het loof alleen / maer de wortel uytgetogen.

19 Of riches and poverty. Van ryckdom en armoede.
POverty seeks craft.

Armoede soeckt list.

Riches long in getting are wholesome,

Langsaem rijckdom is falig,

Light gain makes a heavy purse.

Licht gewin maeckt swear beursen.

Where there is much goods, there are many that eat it,

Waer veel goedt is / daer zijn veel die het eten.

Great house, great cross.

Groot huys groot kruys.

Little ship, little sail.

Kleyn schip / kleyn zeyl.

Little house, little care.

Kleyn huys / kleyn sorgh.

Many Cowes, much trouble.

Deel Koeyen / veel moeyen.

A little hearth, though cold (is good)

That has all one but little wood.

Even kle^nen heert al is hy kout /

Die heeft alleen maer weynigh hout.

A young Courtier, an old beggar.

Iongh hovelingh: out schovelingh.

He that nothing wants is rich:

Although he dwells on the ditch.

Wie niet ontbreeckt is rijck:

Al wont hy aen den dijck.

Rich with little, is like God.

Met weynigh rijck: is Godt ghelijck.

Little with honor, what need you more.

Weynigh met eer / wat hoeftje mere?

Every one knows where the shoe wrings him.

Elck weet waer hem de schoen wringt.

All is not gold that glisters.

Ten is geen goudt al watter blinckt.

No happiness, without adversity.

Geen geluck / sonder druck.

What glistereth that wringeth.

Wat blinckt / dat wringt.

A new shoe can cause pain.

Even nieuwe schoen / kan pijne done.

Even there where men it can not see.

Will often times great sorrow be.

Oock daer men't niet en siet /

Is dickmael groot verdriet.

Every man will wipe his feet upon the poor.

Aen den armen will all man sijn voet wissen.

Every one will go over the longest garden.

Daer de tuyn langst is / will yder over.

When the Salmon is taken the eele sucketh him out.

Als de Salm ghevanghen is / so suyght hem den ael uyt.

When a dog lies under, all the world will scratch him.

Als den hont onder light / al de werelt will hem kretsen.

Men deal ill with him with whom it goes ill.

Men misdeelt die't misgaet.

The last man is bitten of dogs.

Den lesten man byten de honden.

Upon a lean or scabby beast,

All the flies most take their rest.

Op even schrael of schurrift be:

Sitten al de vliegen meest.

Where the causy is lowest the water runs soonest over.

Daer de dijck laeghste is / loopt het water eerst over.

When the stream changes his course men set the beakons in another place.

Als het diep verloopt versetmen de bakens.

When the wolf grows old, then the crows ride him.

Als de wolf out wort / so reyen hem de kraeyen.

Every one is be^ter pleased with a rising than with a falling market,

Yder houdtet mere met de rijsende mart als met de afgaende.

There is but little sorrow for an old cow.

Kleyn is de rou / om even oude koe.

Even hares pull a lion by the beard when he is old.

Oock hasen trecken even Leeuw by den haert als hy out is.

What smarteth teaches.

Wat verseert dat leert.

No man learneth but by hurt or shame.

Niemant leert als met schade of schande.

What does not sour men, does not sweeten them, he what men get not with
trouble is not sweet to them.

Watmen niet en besuert / en besoetmen niet.

What costs nothing is good for nothing.

Wat niet en kost en deught niet.

Blows make wise.

Slagen maken wijs.

After sour comes the sweet.

Nae het zuere komt het soet.

Short branches long vintage.

Korte tacken / langen wijn oegst.

Little wood much fruit.

Weynich houts veel vruchten.

20 Of prosperity. Van voorspoet.
ONe that has all after his wish (or will)

Account him an unhappy man (still.)

Even die't al heeft na sijnen wensch /

Acht dien even ongheluckigh mensch.

Men can bear all things, except good days.

All dingen kan men dragen /

Dytgesondert goede dagen.

When prosperity simileth on thee, stand then on thy watch.

Als 't geluck u lacht:

Staet dan op de wacht.

Men in good condition give good advise.

Menschen in goeden staet / geven goeden raet.

It Is pleasure to see it rain, when one stands in the dry.

It Is geneughelijck te sien regenen / als men in drooge staet,

The best pilotes are a shore.

De best Stuer-luyden zijn aen landt.

It is good steering before wynd and tide.

Voor wint en stroom is it goed stieren.

21 Of thriftines. Van suynicheyt.
SEt thy expense according to thy trade.

Set u teeringe / na u neeringe.

Sparingnes is a great revenue.

Suynicheyt is even groote rent.

Cut your cloak, according to your cloth.

Snyt u Mantel naer u Laken.

Spoiling is a bad custom, Sparing is a sure revenue,

Spillen is even quae gewente

Sparen is even wisse rent.

Green wood, hot bread, and new wine, can not be profitable for the house.

Groen hout / haet broot / en nieuwe Wijn /

En kan voor 't Huys niet dienstigh zijn.

The throat costs much.

De keel kost veel.

When the season gives new increase, Be not the^^ too hasty in buying: But
tarry a little if thou be wise For it differs the half in prise.

Wanneer de tijdt geeft nieu gewas /

Weest dan in 't koopen niet te ras.

Maer toeft even weynich fie die wijs.

Want 't scheelt de he^ft well in de prijs

Velvet and silk are strange bearbs, they blow the fire out of the kitchen. To
be lazy, dainty, and to love to eat much, are three things which are good for
nothing.

Fluweel en Zijde is zeltsaem kruyt /

Het blust het byer de keucken uyt.

Luy en lecker en veel te meugen /

Zijn dry dingen die niet en deughen.

Spare some money in the half empty vessel: But saving will not help when the
vessel is empty,

In 't halfleegh vat / gelt sparen wat /

Maar voor lege vaten kan 't sparen niet baten.

22 of labor and diligence. Van arbeyt en naersticheyt.
VVIsdome increases by diligence.

Wijfheyt neemt toe door vlijticheydt.

He that esteems not a penny, will not be master of guldens.

Die geen penning / en acht; en wordt geen guldens here.

Stockfish is made soft with much beating.

Met veel slagens wordt de Stock visch morwer.

Small fish sweet fish.

Kleyn visje / soet visje.

Little gain^ brings in wealth.

Kleyn ghewin / brengt rijckdom in.

By little and little ste^king, the tree falls.

Allen^se slagen / valt be boom.

Many hands make light work.

Veele handen maecken licht werck.

Many littles make a mickle.

Deel kleyntjes maken even groot.

Soft and fair goes far.

Sachtgens en foetgens gaet verde,

Nothing so hard but by diligence may be overcome.

Niet so swaer of men kant met neersligheydt ove^winnen.

Labor is profitable for the body.

Arbeyt is voor het lichaem profijtelijck.

God gives the fowls meat but they must fly for it.

Godt geeft de voghelen de kost / maer sy moetender om vlieghen.

He becomes poor that deals with a slack hand: but the hand of the diligent
makes rich. Pro 10.4.

Die met even bedrieghelijcke handt werckt / wort arm:

Maer de hant der vlijtighen maeckt rijck.

23 of Idleness. Van ledigheyt.
POverty (...) the reward of idleness.

Armoede is luyheyts loon.

He that in his land no come does sow:

Shall truly (none other but) thistles mow.

Wie in sijn lant geen koren saeyt:

It Is seker / dat hy distels maeyt.

Of idleness comes no goodness.

Dan leedigheyt komt niet goedts.

An idle person is the devils pillowe.

Even ledigh mensch is duyvels oorkussen.

No sheep runs into the mouth of a sleeping wolf.

Den slaepende wolf en loopt gheen schaep in den mont.

A flying crow catches some what.

Even vliegende kraey vangt wat.

Idleness nourishes all evil:

To do some what is better Counsel.

Leedigheyt voet all quaet:

Wat te done is beter raet.

If the mill finds no corn, it grindeth stones.

Vindt de meul geen koren / so maeltse steenen:

Idleness is famines mother.

And of theft (it is) full brother.

Leedigheytis hongers moeder:

En van diefte volle broeder,

Rest makes rustie.

Rust maeckt roest.

A plough that works, glistereth:

But the still water stinketh.

Even ploegh die werckt / blinckt:

Maer 't stille water stinckt.

To do nothing reaches to do evil.

Niet done / leert quaet done.

Because of the winter the sluggard will not plow: therefore shall he beg in
harvest, but there shall be nothing (for him) Prove. 20.4.

Om den winter en sal de luyaert niet ploeghen: daerom sal hy bedelen in den
oogst / maer daer en sal niet zijn.

24 Of jesting. Van jockinge.
HE that jesteth inticeth.

Die jockt / die locked.

It 's ill jesting with edged tools.

It Is quaet gecken met scherp gereetschap.

He that will jest must bear jesting, else it were better let alon^.

Die jocken will / moet jock verstaen:

'T is anders beter ongedaen.

An ape will be mocking with every one although she can not cover her own arse.

Even aep w^l met even ^eder gecken:

Maer kan haer eygen aers niet decken.

25 Of rebukes. Van berispinge.
A Scabbed head fears the comb.

Even schurrift hooft ontsiet de kam.

Touch a gald horse and he will kick.

Raeckt even be feert peert aen / en hy sal slaen.

Clawe me; and I Will claw thee.

Craewt my en ick kraeuwdy.

He that builds upon the high way has many that carpe at him.

Die aen den wegh timmert / heeft veel berichts.

He had need of a good advocate that is called to every man's sessions.

Die behoeft well even goede voorspraeck / die voor all man's vyerschaer
betrocken wort.

Who is i^ that remains uncensurd, if he speak or write for the world

Wie is it die sonder op spraec blijft /

Die voor de werelt spreeckt of schrijft?

He is wise that is always wise.

Hy is wijs / die altijt wijs is.

A master may miss.

Het mist even meester well.

No plot so crafty but her nest may be once robbed.

Geen so loosen exter of haer nest wort well eens gherooft.

No hen so witty but she lays one eg lost in the nettles.

Geen so snegen hin / of sy leyt well even ey verloren in de netelen.

A good fisher may let slip an eele.

Even goede visscher ontglipt well even ael.

A shod mare may stumble.

Even beslagen merry struyckelt well.

A good gunner may miss^.

Even goet Schutter mist well.

None so wise, but he may fail.

Niemant so wijs / of hy kan falen.

It happens (some time) that a good Seaman falls over board,

'tGebeurt well / dat even goed Zeeman over boort valt.

He is a good gunner who always hits the mark.

It Is even goedt Schutter die altijt het wit raeckt.

He that has an head of butter will come near none oven.

Die even hooft van boter heeft en will by gheen oven komen.

Bad eyes can endure no light.

Quade ooghen konnen geen licht verdraghen.

Slight gold will not be touched.

Slecht gout en will niet getoutst wesen.

He that has a Scabby head will suffer no combing.

Die even schurft hooft heeft / will geen kammen lijden.

He that does evil hates the light.

Die quaet doet / haet het licht.

A scabby horse fears the curry comb.

Even schurft-paert vreest den ros-kam.

An unsound body will suffer no shaking.

Even meeps-lijf will geen beweginghe lijden.

He that reproves a scorner, gets to himself shame; and her that rebukes
the wicked, (gets himself) his blot. Rebuke not a scorner least he hate
thee: rebuke a wise man and he will love thee.

Wie den spotter tuchticht / behaelt sich schande; end die den Godtloosen
bestraft / sijne schand vlecke. En bestraft den spotter niet / op dat by u niet
en haete: bestraft den wijsen / end he sal u lief hebben / Pro. 9.7, 8.

26 Of injury. Van ongelijck.
NO man shall prosper long with evil doing.

Niemant sal lang voorspoet hebben / met quaad done.

Do no man wrong first.

Doet niemant eerst ongelijck

It Is better to suffer wrong, than to do it to another.

It Is beter ongelijck te lijden / als even ander aen te done.

Unjust Substance enricheth not.

Onrecht veerdich goet en rijckt niet.

So gotten, so spent.

So gewonnen so vedteert.

Lightly come, lightly gone.

Licht gekomen licht gegaen.

Men get no profit by cousenage.

Men doet geen voordeel met bedrogh.

A false balance is an abomination to the Lord: but a just weight is his
delight. Pro. 11.1.

Even bedrieghelijcke weech-schale is den Here even grouwel maer even volkomen
weech-steen is sijn well gevallen.

27 Of time, and oppertunity. Van tijdt en gelegentheyt.
THe time that 's past, comes not again.

De tijdt die voorby is / en komt niet weer.

First come, first served (grindeth.)

Die eerst komt / die eerst maelt.

Men must catch when the time is.

Men moet grijpen als tijt is.

Men must set out their tub^ while it raineth.

Men moet sijn tobben uyt setten terwijl het regent.

Men must sail while the wind serves.

Men moet zeylen terwijl de wint dient.

The oppertunity stands out still before any man's door.

Het geluck en staet niet still voor yemants deur.

Land purchase, and good marriage, happens not every day.

Lant kopen en goet houwelijck done / en verschijick all dagh niet.

Use time while time is.

Gebruyckt den tijt terwijl het daer is.

The cat w^ll eat fish, but she will not touch the water.

De kat will visch eeten / maer sy will het water niet raecken.

It Is bad combing where there is no baire.

'T is quaat kemmen daer gheen ha^ren is.

It Is bad making fromity of water allone.

It Is quaat bry maken van water alleen.

It Is bad making cakes without fire or fat.

It Is quaat koecken backen sonder vyer of vat.

A good fire makes a quick cook.

Even goed vyer maeckt even snellen kock.

It Is bad grinding without water.

It Is quaat slijpen / sonder water.

When old dogs bark, its time to look out.

Als oude honden bassen is it tijt uyt te sien.

When thy neighbors house burns its time to look about thee

Als a bueemans huys brant / is it tijt uyt te sien.

28 Of Contentation. Van vergenoeginghe.
EAst, west, at home is best.

Oost / west / t'hu is best.

Often removing costs much bed-straw

Veel verhuysen kost veel bed-stroo.

There grows no cobw^b upon the comb of a mill that is always turning.

Daer wast gheen raegh aen even draeyende meulen kam.

A Rolling stone gathers no moss.

Even rollende steen wort met geen groen gewassen.

Trees that are often replanted prosper seldom.

Boomen die men veel verplant gedyen seldom.

An unconstant man prospers not.

Even looper en gedijt niet.

Stability causes prosperity.

Blijven doet beclijven.

Not to throw away our old Shoes before we have new.

Geen oude Schoenen wech werpen / eer men nieuwen heeft.

Godliness is great riches if a man be content with what he has,

Godtsalicheydt is groote rijckdom als men te vreden is met het geene men heeft.

29 of Contention and unity. Van twist en eenigheyt.
LOve peace.

Hebt de vreede lief.

Shun contention and pleading.

Schuwt het twisten en pleyten.

The truth is lost with too much contention.

Met al te veel krackeelens / wordt de waerheydt verloren.

Contention brings decaie.

Twist verquist.

Concord (o^ agreement) makes strong.

Eendracht geeft macht.

Agreement can do very much

Eenigheyt vermach veel.

Better is a dry morsel, and quietness therewith, than an house full of
sacr^fi^es with strife Pro. 17.1.

Eene drooghe beat / end rust daer by / is beter / dan even Huys vol van
geslachte beesten / met twist.

30 of lying. Van leugen.
HAte lying.

Haat de leugen.

The mouth that lies, kills the soul.

De mont die lieght / die doodt de Ziel.

Show me a liar, and I Will show thee a thief.

Wijst my even leughenaer / en ick wijse u even dief.

A liar must have a good memory.

Even leugenaer moet even goede memory hebben.

The getting of treasures by a lying tongue, is a vanity tossed to and fro of
them th^^ seek death. Pro. 21.6.

Te arbeyden om schatten met even valsche tonghe / is even voortgedrevene
ydelheyt der gener, die den doodt soecken.

31 Of women, love, woeing, marriage, and duties of man and wife. Van
vrouw-menschen, liefde, vryen, trouwen, en plichten tusschen man en wijf.
A Virtuous woman is a Crown to her husband: but she that makes ashamed is as
totrennes to his bones. Pro. 12.4.

Even kloecke Huys brouwe is even kroone hares Heeren: maer die beschaemt maeckt
/ is als verrottinghe in sijne beenderen.

A woman fair and wine that 's sweet.

Are full of poison (though) secret.

Even schoone Vrouw' en soete wijn /

Die zijn vol heymelijck fenijn.

Married in have repented at leisure.

Haest getrout / lang berout.

Of early breakfast, and late marriage, men get not lightly the headache.

Van vroeg ontbyten / en laet te trouwen / en krijght men niet licht den hooft
sweer.

He that asks timerously learneth to deny.

Wie beschromelijck vraeght / die leert weygeren.

By labor men get fire out of a stone.

Met arbeyt krijghtmen vyer uyt den steen.

The constant hun^er catches the dear.

De stadighe jagher vangt het wilt.

Importunity does obtain.

Aenhouden doet verkrijghen.

That wh ch is gotten with trouble is possessed with love.

Dat met moyte verkregen is / wordt met minne beseeten.

He that will lay out but little, seldom buyeth good flesh.

Die weynigh besteden wilt / seldom goed vleesch koopt.

They who with loves dart pierced be,

Can neither spot nor defect see.

Die van de liefde zyn gesteeken /

En sien noch vlecken noch ghebreken.

In love is no lack

Im liefde en is gheen ghebreck.

Love is blind and cannot see.

Liefde is b'int en kan niet sien.

It Is best to woe where a man can see the smoke.

't Is best te brijen / daer men de roock kan sien.

Beauty is but dirt if honesty be lost.

Schoonherdt is maer drec als d'eerbaerheydt verloren is.

Women and pears that do not crack men esteem to taste the best.

Vrouwen en peeren die niet en kraecken.

Die achtmen alderbest te smaken.

Bad legs and good wives, ought to stay within doors.

Quade beenen en goede wijven.

Dienen well in huys te blijven.

Much on the street causes a bad Name.

Veel op de straet: licht op de praet.

Cleanly clothed: and not too gawdie.

Reyn gekleedt: en niet te breedt.

See not husbands, be blind ye wives, that shall preserve the house in quiet.

En siet niet mannen weest blint ghy Drouwen /

Dat sal het huys in rusten houwen.

Good speeches for bad words, set many a froward pate at peace.

Op quade woorden / goede reden /

Stelt menigh korsel hooft te vre^den.

No wagon rides so softly, which sometimes suffers not a jog,

Geen wagen oyt so facht en reet /

Die somtijts niet even stootje leet.

It Is a greeat sorrow in the house, where the hen crows, and not the cock.

It Is in het huys even groot verdriet /

Daer 't hintje kraeyt / en't haentje niet.

The wives virtue is the husbands honor.

Man's eere Vrouwen deught

Neither reprove nor flatter thy wise, where any one hears or sees it.

En straft of streelt u Vrouwe niet /

Daer 't jemant hoort of jemant siet.

The eye of the master makes the horse fat?

The eye of the mistres makes the chambers near.

Het ooge van den Here dat maeckt de peerden vet /

Het ooge van de Vrouw dat maerkt de kamers net.

They that use the looking glass often, spin seldom.

Wie veeltijts spiegelen seldom spinnen.

A continual dropping in a very rainy day, and a contentious woman are alike.
He that hides her hides the wind, and the ointment of his right hand which
bewrays (it self) pro, 27.15, 16.

Eene geduyrige druypinge ten dagh des slach-regens end even kijfachtighe
Huys-vrouwe zijn even gelijck. Elck even diese verberght / soude den wint
verberghen / end de olye sijner rechterhant die roept.

32 Of have and sobriety. Van haesticheyt en sachtmoedicheyt.
Have makes wast.

Haest verquist.

Hasty speed is seldom good.

Haestige spoedt / is seldom goet.

Folly has eagles wings but owls eyes.

De dwaes^ert heeft arents vleugelen / maer uyls ooghen.

Hasty questions must have slow answers.

Op haestige vragen dient traegh geantwoordt.

Hasty men ought to ride on asses

Iachtige menschen dienen op Ez else te tijden.

He that creeps falls not.

Die kruypt en valt niet.

Men come to their journies end with going easily,

Met goed gemack raecktmen oock voort.

Soft and fair goes far.

Al sachtgens en foetgens gaende / raecktmen verre.

A soft fire makes sweet malt.

Even sacht veertjen maeckt soete mout.

Ride on, but look about.

Rijt voort maer siet om.

Have is no speed.

Haest is geen spoet.

More have than good speed.

Mere haeft dan goeden spoet.

Speedy Counsel seldom profitable.

Snelle raet / seldom baet.

Of hasty advise, never (came) good action.

Van snellen raet / noyt goede daet.

The tailor that makes no knot, loses his stitch,

De nayer die geen knoop en leyt / verliest sijn steeck.

Measure thrice ere thou cut once.

Meet driemael eer ghy eens snijt.

Who so oveneth in have, gets horned bread home.

Wie in der haest ovent / krijght gehorende brooden t'huys.

Before you ride on look to your girths.

Eer ghy voort rijt / fiet na de linze.

Make trial first, and then weigh.

Eerst wickt / dan waegt.

The candle that goes before gives best light.

De keerse die voorgaet / licht best.

Nothing in bast but to catch fleas.

Geen dingen metter haest als vloon te vangen.

With time and straw the medlers ripen.

Met tijt en stroo rijpen de mispelen.

In time a mouse will byte a cable in pieces.

Metter tijt bijt de muys even kabel in stucken.

Time brings roses forth.

De tijt brengt roosen voort.

In time the corn ripeneth.

Metter tijt rijpt het koren.

The diligent hand and sparing tooth buyeth other folks land.

De neerstighe hand / en sparige sant / coopt ander luy lant.

The water in time makes a hole in an hard stone.

Hot water door tijt holt even harden steen.

He that will make a golden gate, must every day, bring a nail (thereto).

Die even goude poorte will maken / brenghter elcken dagh even naghel.

The thoughts of the diligent tend only to plentiousnes: but of every one that
is bastie, only to want. Pro. 21.5.

De gedachten des vlijtigen zijn alleen tot overschot: maer eens yeders die
haestigh is / alleen tot gebreck.

33 of promises. Van beloften.
PRomise not lightly.

En belooft niet lichtelijck.

Perform what thou have promised,

Houd dat ghy belooft hebt.

An honest man is as good as his word.

Even eerlijck man is so goede als sijn word.

An honest man's word is as good as his bond.

Het woordt van even eerlijck man is so goet als fijn obligatie.

It Is certainly a poor man that cannot promise fair.

Het is voorwaer even armen man /

Die niet wat schoons beloven kan.

Fair promises, foul performances.

Schoone beloften vuyle volbrenginghen.

34 of friendship and confidence. Van vrientschap en vast-betrouwen.
PRove thy friend and try thy sword, which will be worth great treasure to
thee.

Beproeft u vrient / beproeft u sweert:

Dat is u groote schatten weert.

Loss breaks friendship.

Schade schent vrientschap.

That dog from whom men take a bone respects no friends.

Die hont diemen even been ontneemt en kent geen vrienden.

In the parting of the inheritance friendship stands still.

In It deylen van't erf / staet de vrientschap stille.

Nephew so long as I give.

Neef so langh ick geef.

A friend is known in need, the richer are known after death.

Den vrient die kentmen in der noot /

Den rijcker kentmen na de doot.

A friend in need is a friend indeed.

Even vriendt in noot / is even vriendt inder daet.

Thrust not thy finger in a fools mouth.

Steeckt u vinger in geen dwafens mont.

With fools men must not play the fool.

Met gocken en moet men niet dwasen.

If thou give a staff to a fool, surely he will strike thee in the neck.

So ghy even stock geeft aen even geck /

Gewis hy slaet u in den neck.

Too much trusting makes many to repent.

Te veel betrouwen: doet veel berouwen.

Before thou trust a friend, eat a peck of salt with him.

Al eer dat ghy even vrient betrout /

So eet hem met even mudde sout.

If thou offer a fool thy fingers, it is strange if he take not the fist.

So ghy even geck de vingers biet /

It Is vreemdt neemt hy de vuysten niet.

Give a fool an inch, and he will take an clue.

Geeft even sot even taely / en hy sal even elle nemen.

35 Of discretion. Van bescheydenheydt.
It Is bad catching hares with drums.

It Is quaet hasen met trommels vangen.

All birds shun the open net.

All vogels schouwen d'openbare netten.

He that spits against the wind, makes his beard foul.

Wie tegen de wint spouwt / maeckt sijn baerdt vuyl.

36 of secrecy. Van verborgentheden.
THere is nothing secret that shall not be revealed.

Daer en is niet verborghen / dat niet openbaer en word.

The truth that lay in the dark comes clearly to light.

De waerhe^t die in duyster lagh /

Die komt met klaerhe^t aen den dagh.

Although a lie be finely clothed, yet it hu^^eth its master.

S^ is de leugen schoon bekleedt:

Sy doet noch haren meester leet.

That comes to light at last that lay hidden under the snow.

Het komt ten lesten aen den dagh /

Wat in de sneeu verholen lagh.

Men see at last by the dung who has eaten the medlars.

Men siet ten lesten aen den stront wie de mispels gegeten heeft.

37 of necessity. Van nootsakelijckheyt.
NEed causes the cat to put forth her foot.

With noot roert de kat haer poot.

The bitings of dying beasts are mortal.

De beten van stervende gedierten zijn doodelijck.

To force an enemy into a strait,

Makes him many times escape:

In engte zijnen vyand dringen /

Doet hem menichmael ontspringen.

When thine enemy retreateth, make freely a golden bridge for him.

Als u vyand gaet te rugh /

Maeckt hem vry even gulden brug.

Necessity has no law.

Het nood wendigheyt heeft geen wet.

Need makes the old wife trot.

De noot doet even out wijf draven.

Need drives.

Noot stoot

When the water runs into any ones mouth, then learns he first to swim.

Als yemandt 't water in den mondt loopt / dan leert hy eerst swemmen.

No gold so red; but it must out for bread.

Geen gout so root: of moet uyt om broot.

Hunger eats through stone walls.

Honger eet door steene mueren.

No better masters than poverty and need

Geen beter meesters als armoed en noot.

Diligent searching comes from poor fo^ks.

Naeu ondersoecken komt van arm lieden.

38 of retribution. Van weder-looninge.
WHat thou do to another shall be don to thee.

Gelijck ghy even ander doet / sal u geschieden.

As thou have sowed so shall thou reap

Ghelijck als ghy sult ghesaeyt hebben / so sult ghy oock maeyen.

He that does well, shall find well.

Die well doet / die well vint.

He is fallen into the pit which himself has made.

Hy is in de kuyl ghevallen / die hy selfs ghemaeckt had.

He has plucked the net over his own head.

Hy heeft hemselfs het net over het hooft gehaelt.

So gotten, so spent.

So gewonnen / so verteert.

As it came, so it is gone.

Zoo 't quam / zoo 't voer.

39 of service. Van dienst.
THere is much to be learned of froward masters.

By moeyelijcke Heeren / is veel te leeren.

It must be a wise hand that shall sheere a fools head well.

'T moet even wijse handt zijn die even sotten kop well scheere sal.

What hinders that teaches.

Wat let dat leert.

Men have need of great skill to give content to a fool.

Men heeft groote kunste van done /

Om even narre te voldoen.

He must rise betimes that will please every body.

He moet vroegh op staen die all man believen will,

40 Iournie-speeches. Reys-spreuken.
NO man is esteemed in his own Country.

Niemant is in weerd; in sijn eygen eerd.

He that is nipped here and there, and often pulled by the nose; though he
were dull, he should be sharpened.

Die hier en daer eens wordt genepen /

En dickwils by de neus gegrepen;

Al is hy plomp / hy wort gheslepen.

Hard stones sharpen iron:

Hard thrusts make wiser.

Hard steenen slijpen yser:

Hard stooten maken wijser.

Every bird praises its own nest.

Even yder voghel prijst sijn nest.

Home is home though never so homely.

T'huys is t'huys al is it noch so slecht.

Travail east or travail west,

A man's own house is still the best.

Vaert ghy dan oost / of vaerje west /

Eens eygen huys is alderbest.

Dogs have teeth in all Countries.

Honden hebben tanden in all landen.

A man must not ride a free horse to death.

Even willigh paerdt en moet men niet over rijden.

A tired horse sees a foul stable rather than a fair way.

Even vermoeyt peert siet liever even vuylen stal als even schoonen wegh.

41 of imitation and likeness. Van navolginge en gelijckheyt.
THe servaunt is like his master.

De knecht gelijckt sijn meester.

Like master, like servaunt.

Sulcke Here / sulcke knecht.

Birds of one feather, will fly together.

Vogelen van eender veeren vliegen geern to samen.

Like will to like, be they poor or rich.

Elck sijns gelijck / 't sy arm of rijck.

Unequal horses draw badly.

Ongelijcke peerden trecken qualijck.

Young cats will mouze:

Young apes will louze.

Katte-jonghens willen muysen:

Ape-jonghens willen luysen.

42 of honor, offices, and matters of state. Van eere, ampten, en saecken van
State.
When apes will (adventure to) climb too high,

Then men their naked buttocks first epsy.

Als apen hooge klimmen willen /

Dan sietmen eerst haer naeckte billen.

A man is not known before that he comes to honor.

Men kent even man niet eer /

Voor dat hy komt tot eer.

Set a beggar on horseback and he will ride a pace.

Set even bedelaer te Paert en hy sal draven.

Men know a man's wisdom when he is. an head

Men kent even man's betalen als hy gelooft is

Men kent even man's gedult als hy in noot is

Men know a man's humility when he is. great

Men kent even man's nedericheyt als hy groot is

Men kent even man's rijckdom als hy doot is

Smiths children are used to sparks.

Smits kinderen zijn well voncken gewoon.

Many cooks salten the pottage.

Veel kocken versouten den bry.

At much command, is least don. or Least is don when many command.

Aen bele belast wordt minst gedaen.

Common goods are oftenest lost.

Gemeen goed gaet meest verloren.

Coupled sheep drown (one another).

Ghekoppelde schapen die verdrencken,

Many sheepheards with the sheep,

Will but the longer sleep.

Veel herders by de Schapen /

Sul en maer te langer slapen.

Common estate, none estate:

Gemeen goet / geen goet.

It Is needles to have two great masts on one ship.

Twee groote masten op even Schip en dienen niet,

The pastor and Sexton seldom agree.

Pastoor en Coster zijn seldom eens.

Who so climbeth higher than becomes him, he falls lower than he wishes.

Wie hooger klimt a's't hem betaemt /

Die valt well lager als hy raemt.

After high f^oods (come) low ebs.

Nae hooge vloeden diepe ebben.

He that exalts his gate seeks destruction. Pro. 17.19.

Die sijn deure verhoogt / soeckt verbrekinghe.

Favor seedeth arts.

Gunst voet kunst.

What is shameful though it be hidden, yet can it not at all be accounted
honorable.

'T gene dat schandelijck is / alhoewel het verborgen wordt / so en kan het
nochtans geensins eerlick geacht werden.

Honor once lost returns no more.

Verloren eer / keert nimmermeer.

When gentlemen begin to domineer then countrymen come to loss.

Als de jonckers b'indt rousen / dan moeten de boeren ha^r laten.

Whensoere a Prince leaps out of the band:

Often therefore suffers all the land.

Wanneer even Prins springt uyt de bant.

Daerom lijt dickmael al het landt.

Men hang the little thieves, and let the great ones escape.

De kleyne diefjens hangtmen / de groote laetmen loopen.

What the sow does, the pigs are punished for.

Wat de seughe doet: wordt by de bigghen gheboet.

It Is good fishing in troubled waters.

In troubel water is 't goed visschen.

The camel loves to drink when the water is stirred.

De kemel drincktliefst als 't water geroert is.

Where churning is there is fatnes.

In de commelinge is vet.

Men cannot hear laws when the drum is beaten.

Onder den trommel en hoortmen geen wetten.

Robbed masters make rich servants.

Dignity loadeth.

Staet belaet.

Care and watchfulnes are the matters of lord.

43 Mingled speeches. Gemengde spreucken.
THe wrath of God goes forth with a soft pace to the vengeance of it self.

De gramschap Gods gaat met even langsaem tred voort tot het wreken hares selfs.

Honesty is little accounted of.

Dromicheyt wort weynich geacht.

Money is very much esteemed.

'T gelt wort seer well gheacht.

Thou labourest in vain.

Ghy doet verloren arbeyt.

We are all the worse for too much liberty (too much will).

Wy sijn allegaer door te veel wills te slimmer.

Reports are as well feigned and falls as true.

De gheruchten zijn so well versierd end leugenachtigh als waer.

Although strength fail, yet the will is to be praised.

Alhoewel de krachten ontbreken / nochtans moet men de will prijsen.

Those things are most desired which cost most.

Die dingen zijn meest begeerd / die meest kosten.

The dearer, the acceptabler.

Hoe dierder / hoe lieber.

Far fetched and dear bought is meat for ladies.

Iuffrouwen.)

There is nothing that sooner dries up than a tear.

Daer is niet dat eerder opdrooght als even traan.

He that has once bin perjured, must not again be creditted.

Die eens even valschen eedt ghedaen heeft / die moet men daer na niet mere
ghelooven.

It Is an honorable shame to dye for a good cause.

It Is even eerlijcke schande / voor even goede saecke te sietven.

If thou art feared by many, then have thou also many to fear.

Indien ghy van vele wordt ontsien / so hebt ghy oock vele te vreesen.

He who names any man unthankful, he names all evil in him.

Die jemant ondanckbaer noemt / die noemt all ghebreken in hem.

The ungodly cannot prosper.

Den godloosen en kan't niet well gaen.

To err is humane: but they are fools that persevere in their error.

Dwaelen is menschelijck: maer 't zijn sotten die in haer doolinghe volherden.

One mischance comes not alone.

Even ongeluck komt niet alleen.

A good beginning is good: but the end must bear the burden.

Even goed begin is goed behagen: maer 't eynde sal de last dragen.

We live all by one God, but not by one mind.

Wy leven al by even Godt / maer niet by even sin.

Many men have many minds.

Veele menschen hebben veele sinnen.

No man can content all men.

Niemant kant all man se pas maecken.

He that thrusts his head in every hole may lightly lose his ears.

Die 't hooft licht steeckt in all gaten /

Die kander licht sijn ooren laten.

What the eye sees not, the heart desires not.

Wat het ooge niet en siet /

Dat begeert het heart niet.

There is no hunting with unwilling dogs.

Met onwillige honden is it niet te jaghen.

He that has an ill name is half hanged.

Die in even quaedt geruchte komt / is half gehangen.

Money answers all things.

Het ghelt verantwoort alles.

Pennyes reason sounds best.

Penninc^ reden klinckt best.

Money that 'i dombe, makes that which is crooked straight.

Gelt dat stom is: maeckt recht dat krom is.

One quill is better in the hand.

Then seven geese upon the strand (shore).

Even schaft is beter in de hant /

Als seven gansen op de strant.

One bird in the hand is worth two in the bush.

Even vogel inde hant is beter als twee in 't bos.

An old cat plays with no ball.

Even oude kat speelt met geen balleken.

It Is hard cosening an old fox.

Even oude vos is qualijck te bedriegen.

An old rat will not into the trap.

Even oude rat will niet in de val.

It Is ill catching old birds with chafe.

Men can oude vogelen qualijck met kaff vangen.

Although the dog seems not to be too great: yet he takes a mighty swine.

Al schijnt den hont niet te groot te zijn /

Noch vangt hy well even machtigh swijn.

A cat may look upon a King.

Even kat siet well op even Koning.

He is little indeed, that can do no hurt.

Hy is well kleyn die niet kan schaden.

It Is better to have a dog ones friend than foe.

It Is beter even hont te brient / als te brant hebben.

That which has horns will sting.

Wat hoorenen heeft will stinghen.

A very gnat can hurt the sight of a Lion.

Even mugghe kan selfs aen de Leeuw' het ghesichte quetsen.

Little undertaking great rest.

Luttel ouderwints / groote rust.

Hoe edelder heart / hoe buyghsamer hals.

Liberty is Ioyfulnes.

Dryheyt blyheydt.

Death spares neither young nor old.

De doot spaert jongh noch out.

9.27.

It Is all menschen geset eenmael te sterven / end daer na het oordeel.

44 Good counsel in several cases. Goede raden in verscheyde saken.
TAke not that in hand, which thou may repent hereafter.

Neemt niet by der hant dat u hier na mocht rouwen.

Never give thy mind lost.

Geeft nimmermeer de moet verloren.

i. e.

Give not over to hope well.

Laet niet as well te hoopen.

Hout op van scherpelijck te vraghen na't gene u niet aan en gaat.

All that thou see do not judge

Al dat ghy siet en oordeelt niet

All that thou hear do not believe.

Al dat ghy hoort en gelooft niet

All that thou know do not speak

Al dat ghy weet. en seght niet

All that thou can do not do.

Al dat ghy meught en doet niet

45 Christian remembraunces. Christelijcke bedenckinghen.

where every one searches himself, no man is lost.

Versint / eer ghy begint.

Counsel before action.

Dialogues and ordinary discourses among men.
TO samen-sprekingen en gemeyne coutingen onder de menschen.
Morning salutations.
A Good morrow Sir.


B And you also Sir.


A Good morrow neighbor.


B And to you also my loving neighbor.


A God give you good morrow Bernard.


P And you also Austin: God give you good morrow.


A Good morrow be to you.


B I thank you Sir.


A I wish you a good morrow.


B I wish the like also to you.


A I wish this day may be prosperous to you.


B And I wish it may not go il with you.


A What do you up so early?


B Is it not time to be up?


A Wherefore do you rise so soon?


B To rise betimes in the morning is the wholesomest thing in the world.

B End u oock mijn Here.

B End u need Augustijn: go^den dach geve u Godt.


A Goeden dach zy u. l.


B Ick bedancke u mijn Here.


A Ick wensch u goeden dach.


B Ick wensche u desghelijcx.


A V moet desen dach well zijn.


B 'Ten moet u oock niet qualijck gaen.

B Isset niet tijdt op telzijn?


A Waerom staet ghy so vroegh op?


B S'morghens vroegh op te staen / is het ghesondste ding in de werelt.


2 Salutations at meeting and parting.
C God save you David.


D And you also Clemens.


C God save you heartily.


D And you also, as heartily.


C How do you?


D I am well I thank God; at your service: and you Clemens, how is it with you?
well?


C I am also in health: how does your father and mother?


D They are in health praised be God.


C How goes it with you my good friend?


D It goes well with me, goes it but so well with you.


C I wish you good health.


D I wish the same to you also.


C I salute you.


D And I you also.


C Are you well? Are you in good health?


D I am well. Indeed I am in good health. I am healthful, and in prosperity.


C That is good. That is well. That is pleasing to me. That makes me glad. I
love to hear that. I beseech you to take care of your health. Preserve your
health.


D I can tarry no longer now. I am in have to be gone. I must go. I have need
of of my time. I cannot abide standing here. Fare you well. God be with you.
God keep you still. I wish your health may continue


C And you also my loving friend God protect you. God guide you. God be with
you. May it please you in my behalf, heartily to salute your wife and children.


D I will do your message: But I pray commend me also to your father and
mother.

D End ick u oock.

3 Salutations for the evening tide and night.
E Good even my friend.


F you are well come Edward: I am glad to see you. How is it with your whole
family? come you now from home?


E yea, I came even now from home, and have left al in good health for so much
as I know: and am come hither to visit you mine old acquaintance.


F That is very well don: friends ought to be friendly. I am bound highly to
thank you for your so great love and remembrance of us; I wish that I may
deserve, and if it be possible, again require it.


E Forbear I pray you to complement so. I have do you no such great
friendship, but you have done ten times more for me. But I can not tatry here.
I must return home, for it begins to be late and dark My friend Francis, I
wish you a good even.


F I thank you hartelle: and I wish you the same with a good heart. But what
have have you? It is not so late as it seems to be: for the days begin to
shorten.


E Although it were not late, yet I must be at another place of an errand,
before I can go home.


F Go to, I will not detain you. Only I wish this evening may be prosperous
to you.


E And I wish it may not be unprosperous to you.


Another.
G What is the clock? what time a night is it?


H It is ten a clock. It has stricken ten. It is almost ten a clock.


G I know it not. I think it is not so late. It cannot be so late.


H It is indeed. It is surely. I have heard it strike.


G Then it is time to go to bed, We must then go to sleep. We must then
depart, and go to rest.


H I am not sleepie. I have at present no need of rest. I am not sleepie. I am
very wakefull.


G But I am very sleepie. I have great need of rest. I am very sleepie. I
cannot hold open mine eyes. I bid you therefore good night my friend. God give
you good night.


H Go then to sleep: and God keep you. I wish this night may be prosperous to
you. I wish you a good night. I wish this night may further you, and that you
may sleep soundly.


G I thank you for all your kindness. God be with you.


H But stay a little. Me thinks you do much forget your self. Ought we not
first to pray to God together?


G I thank you for your remembrance. If it please you to perform the duty, I
shall join with you willingly.


H Go to, I will do it for this time by Gods help.


Evening prayer.
O Merciful God, eternal light shining in darkness, thou who expellelt the night
of sin and all blindness of heart: seeing thou have ordained the night to rest,
as the day to labor, we beseech thee grant, that our bodies may rest in
peace and quiet, that afterward they may be fit to undergo the labor which
they must endure. Moderate out sleep, that it be not disorderly, that we may
remain unspotted both in body and soul: yea that our sleep it self may be to
thy glory. Englighten the eyes of our understanding, that we may not sleep in
death, but always expect our redemption from this misery. Defend us also
against all assaults of the devil, taking us into thine holy protection. And
forasmuch as we have not passed this day without sinning greatly against thee,
we beseech thee to cover our sins by thy bottomeles mercy, like as now thou
have covered all things on earth with the natural darkness of the night; that
so we may not therefore be cast from thy presence. Grant also rest and
comfort to all sick, sorrowful and assaulted hearts, through our Lord Jesus
Christ, who has thus taught us to pray: Our father. etc.

Het avondt ghebed.
O Barmhertighe Godt / even: which licht schijnende in de duysternisse / ghy die
verdrijft den nacht der sonden end all blin theyt des herten: na dien ghy den
nacht verordineert hebt om te rusten / gelijck den dagh om te arbeyden / wy
bid: den u geeft / dat onse lichame^ in vrede en stilheydt rusten / o^ datse
daer na bequaem zijn moghen / den arbeydt te lijden dien sy draghen moeten.
Matight onsen slaap / dat die niet onordentlijck en zy / op dat wy aen lijf
end siele onbevleckt mogen blijven: ja dat onse slaep selfs gheschiede t^ uwer
eere. Derlicht de ooghen onser verstandts / op dat w^ in den doodt niet en
onslaye^ maar altijt verwachten op onse verlossinghe uyt dese ele^ dicheydt.
Beschermt ons oock voor all aenvechtinghe d^^ duyvels / ons in uw' heylight
gheleyde neemende. End nadien wy desen dach niet toeghebracht en hebben /
sonder teghen u grootelijckx ghesondicht te hebben / wy bidden u^ wilt onse
sonden bedecken doo^ uw' grondeloose barmherticheydt / ghelijck ghy nu all
di^ghen op aerden met natuu^ lijcke duysternisse des nacht^ bedeckt hebt; op
dat wy daer om van uw' aenschijn niet vers^ooten en werden.

Gheeft oock rust end troost aen all krancken / bedroefden end aenghevochten
herte^ door onsen Here Iesum Christum / die ons alsoo heeft leeren bidden:
Onse Vader etc.

3 Childrens talk, of rising up in the morning, and goeing to school and
other familiar things
I Hear you not? rise.


K Let me sleep a little yet.


I How long will you sleep? It is time to rise.


K It is not yet day.


I Open your eyes, and you will see that it is late.


K Tell me truly I pray thee, what a clock it is.


I It will suddenly strike seven: therefore rise presently, or otherwise you
will be chidden of the master. And as you rise, look to it, that you trusse up
your hose close, and tie them round about, so shall you take the less cold.


K Mine eylit-holes are all in pieces.


I Why have you not caused them to be mended?


K I thought not on it


I See that it be don to morrow.


K I will take care of it.


I Do you put on your best coat?


K I thought it had bin my working days one.


I Fit your cloths well. you stretch them too high.


K That adornes well.


I Let us go down now; and let us look before us. But think you not on our
loving Lord?


K We will do that by and by, when we are at church.


I What if some evil befall you in the mean time? Truly you are unthankful.


K Whence do you gather that?


I Know you not that he has preserved you this night?


K What ought a Christian to do herein?


I You must kneel, and with great devotion pray after this manner.


Morning prayer.
LOrd God, heavenly father, we thank thee that thou have so faithfully
watched over us this night; and beseech thee to strengthen us by thy holy
Spirit, who may henceforth guide us: that we may devote this day and all the
days of our life unto all righteousness and holiness, and that whatsoever we
take in hand our eyes may always look to the spreading abroad of thy glory;
yea that we expect all the succes of our intendements only from thy bountiful
band. And that we may obtain such grace from thee, be pleased according to thy
promise to forgive us al our sins, through that holy passion and bloodshedding
of our Lord Jesus Christ: for we are heartily sorrowful for them. Illuminate
our hearts, that we having put off all the works of darkness may walk as
children of the light in a new life in all godlynes. Give also thy blessing to
the preaching of thy divine word. Destroy all the works of the devil,
strengthen all church officers, and governors of thy people. Comfort all
persecuted and distressed hearts, through Jesus Christ thy beloved son, who
has promised us, that thou will assuredly give us all that we beg in his
name, and therefore has taught us to pray after this manner, Our father etc,

K Is that enough?


I Yea, if you could do that with good understanding true faith, and an
upright heart.


K Let us then go to schole now.


I You must first wash your hands, and rinse your mouth: you must also ri^ze
out your throat well with gorgelling; after that dress your head if it be
tangled, and buckle your shoes, if they be unbuckled.


K That is don already.


I Let us now go strait forward through the church, to school.


K But I would break my fast first, for I am yet fasting.


I Do that freely, and forget not first to call upon Almighty God.


K I pray you teach me that also: for I would feign do it always.


I After this manner shall you do it, if you please.


A short prayer before breakfast.
FEed our souls, oh Lord Christ, with thy love, who by thy goodness do
sustain all things that have received life. Grant, Lord, that these thy gifts
may be holylie used by us, as thou the giver of the same art holy. Amen.

K Come now and eat something with me, if you please: you are very welcome.


I Not I, I thank you heartily, it is yet too early for me to break my fast. I
do not use to eat so soon. Or I have broken my fast an hour ago, I can not
fast so long. But I will attend you for your company so long while you eat if
you please.


K I am sorry Sir to make you wait so long upon me, but you know the proverb,
Necessity has no law: and I hope to recompense your patience ere long with the
like attendaunce, if I can but rise soon enough.


I It is no matter Sir, the service is not so great as to have a word spoken of
it.


K Now God be praised for his good gifts; I have eaten enough till noone.


I Much good may it do you, shall we go now?


K Yea willingly. what a clock is it think you?


I About eight.


K That is the right time for to go to school. How much am I obliged to you,
that you have furthered me so much this morning? It is surely a token that you
bear good affection to me: God grant that I may in some kind deserve it
from you.


3 Kinder gespreck, van s'morgens op te staen, school gaen, en andere
gemeynsame saecken.
I HOordy niet? her op.


K Laet my noch even weynigh slapen.


I Hoe lang wilt ghy slapen? Het is tijdt om op te staen.


K Ten is noch geen dagh.


I Doet uwe oogen op / end ghy sult sien dat het laet is.


K Ick bid u seght my in waerheydt wat ure isset.


I Het sal haest seven slaen: daerom staet datelijck op / of anders sult ghy
van den meester bekeven worden: End in it opstaen / sie toe / dat ghy uwe
koussen van op treck / ^n^stelse rontsom / al sosul^ ghy te min couwe hebben.


K Mijn nes^elgaten zijn alin stucken.


I Waerom hebt ghy die niet done vermaecken?


K Ick dachter niet op.


I Maeckt dattet morghen gedaen wort.


K Ick sal't besorgen.


I Doet ghy u besten rock aen?


K Ick meynde dattet mijnen dagelijckschen hadt geweest.


I Schickt u klederen well. Ghy strecktse te hooch waerts.


K Dat ciert well.


I Laet ons nu afgaen / end laet ons voor ons sien. Maer denckt ghy op onse
lieven Here niet?


K Dat sullen wy vlus done als wy in de kercke zijn.


I Of u daerentusschen yet quaet ghebeurde? voorwaer ghy zijt ondanckbaer.


K Waer uyt neemt ghy dat?


I Weet ghy niet dat hy u desen nacht bewae^t heeft?


K Wat behoort even Christen hier in te done.


I Ghy sult gaen knielen / (...) met groot devotie sul^y aldus bidden.


Het morgen-gebed.
Here Godt / Hemelsche Vader / wy dancken u dat ghy desen nacht so
ghetrouwelijck voor ons gewaackt hebt; end bidden u dat ghy ons wi^de stercken
met uwen Heylighen Gheest / die ons voortaen geleyde: dat wy desen dagh /
mitsgaders all de daghen onses ievens moghen besteeder tot all
gherechticheydt end heylicheydt / end wat wy i^ handen neemen / dat onse
o^ghen altijdt sien / om uw' eere te verbreyden; alsoo dat wy all den
voorspoed onses voornemens van uwe mi^de handt alleen verwachten. End op dat
wy sulcke ghenade van u verkrijghen / wildt ons nae uwe beloftenisse /
vergheven all onse sonden / door dat Heylighe lijden end bloedtvergieten
onses Heeren Jesus Christi: want sy zijn ons van herten leedt. Verlicht onse
herten / op dat wy all wercken der duysternisse afgeleydt hebbende / als
kinderen des lichts / in even nieuw leven moghen wandelen in all godsalicheydt.
Geeft oock uwen seghen totte verkondighe uwes goddelijcken woordts. Verstroyd
all wercken des duyvels / sterckt all Kercken-dienaers end overheden uwes
volcks. Troost all vervolghde end benaude herten / doo^ Iesum Christum uwen
lieven Soon / die ons belooft heeft / dat ghy ons alles wat wy in sijnen naam
bidden / seecker^ijck gheven sult / end daerom ons alsoo heeft leeren bidden:
Onse Vader etc.

K Is It so ghenoech?


I Iae / indien ghy dat met goet verstandt / waere gheloove, end even oprechten
heart kost done.


K Laet ons dan nu ter scholen gaen.


I Ghy moet eerst u ha^den wasschen / end u mont spoelen oock moet ghy
gorgelende uwe keel well uytspoelen; daer na reedt u hooft / so het verwerret
zy / end uwe schoenen ghegespen / indiense onghegespt zijn.


K Dat is al gedaen.


I Laet ons nu recht uyt door de Kercke nae der schoolen gaen.


K Maer eerst soude ick well ontbijten / want ick vast noch.


I Doet dat vry / end vergeet niet eer den Almachtighen Godt aen te roepen.


K Ick bid u. l. leert my dat oock / want ick soude het gaerne altijt done.


I Aldus sult ghy het done / als u belieft.


Even kort gebed eermen ontbyt.
SPijst onse zielen / Here Christus / met uwe liefde / die door uwe goedtheydt
alles onderhout dat leven heeft ontfangen. Geeft / Here / dat dese uwe gaven
heylichlijck by ons genuttigt mogen worden / ghelijck ghy der selfde ghever
heyligh zijt. Amen.

K Komt nu end eet wat met my / so het u belieft: ghy zijt seer wellekom.


I Neen ick. Ick danck u hertelijck / het is voor my noch te vroegh om te
ontbyten. Ick ben niet gewent so vroech te eeten, often Ick hebbe over even ure
ontbeeten. Ick en kan so langhe met vasten. Maar so het u belieft sal ick so
lang als ghy eetet na^ geselschap wachten.


K Het is m^ leed Sr. u ^. so lang op my te done wachten maer ghy kent het
spreeck-woort / noot breeckt wet: oock hope ick eerlanghe dese uwe
geduldigheydt met ghelijck opwachten te vergelden / indien ick maer so vroegh
kan opstaen


I Het is geen nood Here het dienst is so groot niet datter even woordt van
behoorde gesproken te worden.


K Godt zy nu ghelooft voor sijne goede gaven; Ick hebbe tot aen den middach
genoech gegeeten.


I Well match het u bekomen. sullen wy nu gaen?


K Iae gaerne. wat ure isset meyn die?


I Omtrent acht.


K Dat is de rechte tijdt om na school te gaen. Hoe seer ben ick aen u.i.
verobligeert / dat ghy my desen morgen so veel geboordert hebt. Het is even
seker teyken dat ghy my goede genegentheyt draget: Godt geve / dat ick het van
u eenighsins verdienen match.


4 Schoole-talke, about writing, lessons, and the things thereunto belonging.
L YOu make good letters, and write very bravely: but do you write now in
earnest, or do you scribble?


M Truly I write in good earnest, for why should I mispend the time? But
wherefore do you ask me that?


L Because I have once seen, that you wrote better, and therefore I marvel how
it comes to pass that now you write worse.


M That is worthy of no admiration, for I want the helps to write well.


L Which be they?


M Good paper, good ink, a good pen: for this my paper (as you see) does
miserably fleet, the ink is waterie and whitish, the pen, is soft and il
prepared: moreover I have also lost my copy.


L Wherefore have you not provided al these things in time?


M I wanted money, and that I want now also.


L You are fallen into that common proverb, He that wants money wants all
things.


M It fares so with me.


L But when do you hope that you shall get it?


M At the next market my father will send it me, or else he will come himself.


L I will help you in the mean time.


M If you can do that, you will do me a great favor.


L Take these six styvers which I lend you, to provide you paper and other
things.


M How truly is that spoken, A sure friend is tried in a doubtful matter? But
what is in your mind, that you do so well for me of your own accord?


L The love of God, which (as Paul says) is shed abroad in our hearts.


M The power of Gods spirit who is the author of that love is wonderful in our
hearts. But I must consider in the mean time how I may be thankful to you.


L It is a small matter: let those thoughts pass, least they hinder you from
sleeping quietly; restore but to me what have lent you, when It is convenient
for you.


M I shall I hope return it to you with the first.


L But what say you of the penknife which I sold you the day before yesterday?
Is it not good enough?


M Yea, it is very good, but (wretch that I am) there wanted little but I had
lost it.


L How, what say you? how happened that?


M When I came without, it sell from me on the street.


L From whence did it sal from you?


M Out of my sheath, which unwittingly I had left open.


L How did you get it a gain?


M I stuck presently a note on the gates of the door; after dinner a boy out of
the fixed form brought it me again.


L Oh that they were every one so faithful who find lost things.


M Indeed there are few which restore, if the matter be but of any worth.


L And yet that is expressly commanded by the word of God.


M Wherefore not? for it is a kind of theft, if any man keep an other man's
matter that is found, if he do but know to whom he must give it again.


L But many think that they do rightly enjoy whatsoever they have sound that is
lost.


M They err very grossly.


L But (that we may return to our begun discourse) what did you give the boy
which found your penknife?


M I gave him an ortgie and some wall-nuts: moreover I praised him, and in few
words admonished him that he must do the same always.


L You did well, for so another time he will restore the rather, if he have
found any thing. But what if you had lost it?


M I should have borne it with good courage, and I would have bought an other.


L Should you so have borne it with good courage?


M Certainly not without some trouble.


L Not with a good courage then, but I will not urge you more strictly.


M we are no divines (Theologants).


L What then?


M Grammar-boyes.
