An obligation for debt.
I C R. of Amsterdam Inkeeper acknowledge and confess by these presents to be
indebted to the worshipful L. H of the same city merchaunt, or the bearer here
of, the sum of five hundred guldens at 20 stuyvers a piece, and that for a
parcel of Borduice wines bought of him and received to my content promiseing
to pay the said sum at May next coming. And for the same I bind my person and
goods present and to come. Renounceing all helps and benefits of law any wise
contrary hereunto, and particulerly telling the law, that general renuntiation
it of no value, except that the spetiall go before.

In witness of the truth, I have subscribed this in Amsterdam this fifteenth of
September 1646. By me C. R.

Even obligatie van schuldt.
ICk C. R herbergier in Amsterdam / bekenne end belijde mits desen schaldich
te wesen den eersamen L. H. koopman der selver stead / often den brengher deses /
de sum van vijf hondert guldens tot 20 stu^vers 't stuck / end dat ter
saecke van even partije Bordeusz wijnen van hem gecocht end tot mijn ghenoeghen
ontfanghen: belovende de selve sum te May eerst komende te betalen. End daer
voor verbinde ick mijnen persoon / end goederen tegenwoordigh end toekomende
/ ontseggende all behulpselen end voordeelen van rechte desen eenichs^^s
teghenstrijdende / end bysonder den rechte segghende / dat gemeyne
ontsegginghe van geender weerden en is / ten zy dat de bisonderen voor gae.

In kennisse der waerheydt / hebbe ick dit onderteeckent binnen Amsterdam desen
vijftienden September. 1646. By my C. R.

Another, somewhat shorter, and with several payments.
I A B. dwelling at Antwerp, acknowledge and confess to be indebted to H. M.
merchaunt dwelling at Vilain, or the bearer hereof, the sum of Thirty pounds
ten shillings and six pence flemmish coin, and that for five English clothes
which I have bought and received of him: of which clothes I hold my self to be
well satisfied. Therefore I promise to pay him or the bearer hereof the said
sum in three payments, to wit Ten pounds in the whitsun fair of Antwerp next
coming, Ten pounds more at the Baumas fair, and the remainder in the cold
fair of Berghen then nex ensueing without any fraud. In witness of the truth I
have etc.

Even ander, wat korrer, end met verscheydene beralinghen.
ICk I. Bwoonende t'Antwerpen bekenne end belijde schu^dich te zijn H. M
coopman woonende te Velaine / often den brenger van desen, de sum van dertich
ponden chien schellingen end ses p^nningen Vlaemsche munte / end dat voor
vijf Enghelsche lakenen die ick van hem ghekocht end ontfanghen hebbe: van
welcke lakenen ick my well vergenoecht houde. Daerom beloove ick hem often den
brengerdeses de voorseyde sum in drije be talinghen te done / te weten thien
ponden in de Antwerpse Pinxter merci eers^ komende / noch thien ponden te
Bamismer^t end de rest in de koude merct van Bergen daer aen volghende sonder
eenigh bedroch. In kennisse der waerheyt hebick etc.

An obligation with surety.
We N. I and I B as surety, acknowledge by these presents to be indebted and
each one of us for the whole and as principal unto A F accepting the same, the
some of 600 Charles guldens of twenty styvers a piece, for a sort of linen
cloth bought by the said N I and received to his content. For which debt I the
said I B stand surety, and make thereof my proper debt, promising as principal
to pay the same unto the said A F or the bearer hereof, within the space of one
year. Renounceing of the exception of the division, ordinis excussionis, and
all others which might stand me in stead against it. Provided that the said N
I. do free and release me therefrom without cost and damage like as I the said
N I promise to do within the space of fifteen months. For which we equally
bind our persons and goods moveable and immovable, present and to come.
Renounceing all helps and benefits of law any wise contrary hereto, and
particulerly telling the law that general renuntiation is nothing worth except
special go before.

In witness whereof we have set here under our hands (signs manual) in
presence of W T and H E as witnesses, this fourth of September in the year
1646. N I. I B.

Even obligatie met borge.
WY N. I. end I. B als borghe / bekenne midts desen schuldich te zijn / end
elck van ons even voor al / end als principael aen A F 't selve aen nemende de
sum van 600 Carolus guldens van twintich stuyvers 't stuck / ter sake van even
soorte linde laken by den selven N I ghekocht end tot sijnen ghenoegen
ontfanghen. Voor welcke schult ick I. B. voorss borge blijve end maecke daer
mijn erghen schult van belovende die als principael aen den selven A F. often
brenger deses binnen den tijdt van even jaer te betalen / ontseggende de
uytneminghen vander divisien ordinis excussionis, end all andere die my daer
teghen soude moghen te stade komen. Behoudelijcken / dat de selve N. I my daer
van kosteloos end schadeloos ontlaste end ontstae gelijckerwijs ick N. I.
voorsz binnen den tut van vijfthien maenden beloove te done. Waer voor wy
ghelijckelijcken onse persoonen end goederen roerende end onroerende /
tegenwoordigh end toekomende verbinden: verwerpende allen behulpselen / end
voordelen van rechte desen eenichsins tegenstrijdende / end bysonder de rechte
segghende dat gemeyne ontsegginghe van gheender waerden en is / ten sy dat
bysondere voorgae.

In kennisse der waerheydt hebben wy onse handt teeckenen hier onder gesteldt
int bywesen. van W. T. end H. B. a's getuygen / desen 4. Septembris anno 1646.
N. I. I B.

An agreement for hire of an house.
I M. E. acknowledge and confess to have demised (or let) to the worshipful W.
O. an house with a garden situate in Leyden in the clear street, called the
thousand seats, next door to ^h^ N; for the term of eight years following,
beginning at May now next coming 1647, and that for the yearly sum of F^fty
and six guldens of twenty styvers a piece, to pay every half year eight and
twenty goldens current money, the first part whereof will be due and shall be paid
at Alhallowes tide or the first of November 1647 or within a month after that
without fraud. Wherewith both parties being contented, the foresaid demiser and
tenant have promised one an other to keep the foresaid condit ons, under bond
of their persons, and goods moveable and immovable present and to come.
Renounceing al helps of law any wise contrary hereunto, and particulerly the
law saying, tha^ general renuntiation is of no worth except that the spetial
go alo^e.

In witness whereof there are made hereof two Chirographies (or instrument,) one
cut out from the other, subscribed by parties on both sides, and written upon
the cutting through with A B C. in presence of N E and F G witnesses the 5 of
April 1647. By me M. E.

An acquittance for house rent.
I R P acknowledge by these presents to have received of the worshipful O T.
the sum of eighty and three guldens for an half years house rent due for the
dwelling house of the said O T sciruat in Peter and James street in Amsterdam
now at May 1646.

In witness of the truth I have hereunto subscribed my sign manual the 10 of
June 1646. By me R. P.

Quijtscheldinge van huys huere.
ICk R P bekenne mits defen ontfangen te hebben vanden eersamen O. T. de sum
van dry en tachentich guldens voor even half jaer huys huere in Mey 1646
verschenen voor het huys daet de voorschreven O T inwoont staende in Pieter
Jacobs straet tot Amsterdam.

In kennisse der waerheyt heb ick mijn bant teycken hier onder ghesieldt den
thienden Iunij 1646. By my R P.

An acquittance for debt.
I A B dwelling at Bridges, acknowledge and confess by these presents to have
received of I G. dwelling at Antwerp, the sum of ten guldens of twenty
styvers a piece, which I lent him (or which he was indebted to me) whereof I
have lost the obligation which was dated the tenth day of April in the year
1644. Of which sum, and of all other debts which he ha^h owed me to this
day, I hold my self well satisfied, and acquit him of al.

In witness whereof I have hereunto set my sign manual in Bridges the fifth of
September 1646. I. B

Quijt-scheldinghe voor even schult.
ICk I B. woonende te Brugge bekenne end belijde mits defen van I G. woonende
tot Antwerpen ontfangen te hebben de sum van thien guldens van twintich
siuybers 't stuck die ick hem geleent had (often die hy my schuldich is
gheweest) waer van ick de obligatie verloren hebbe dat op den tienden dach
Aprilis in 't jaer 1644. gedateert was Door welcke sum end voor all andere
die hy my tot nu toe schuldich is geweest ick my voldaen houde / end hem van
alles qu^tschelde.

In kennisse der waerheydt heb ick mijn handtteecken hier onder ghesteldt
binnen Brugghe den vijfden Septembris 1646. I B.

A clearing of an account.
THis day the fifth of September 1646 have we V F. and G. H. agreed together in
friendship and have reckoned from the beginning to the end for certain
disbursed moneys, diet, chamber rent, and otherwise, which I V. F demanded and
he remained indebted to me by the end of the account for the sum of 25
guldens, which I acknowledge to have received, and by this all our reckonings
are dead and to nothing, and all that was standing out between us satisfied.
Acted in Amsterdam in the ^o^s of A. R in pr^s^pher of A. B and N. ^. ^.
witness^^ the Fifth of September 1646. V. F G. H.

Even af-rekeningh.
OP huyden den vijfden Septembris 1646. zijn w^ D. F. end G H. minnelijck over
even ghekomen / end van alles tot alles afgherekent voor verschoten penninghen
/ mondt kosten / kamer huer / end andersins / die ick D. F. was e^sschende /
end hy my ^ot slot van rekeninghe schuldich bleef voor de sum van 25 ^uldens
/ welcke sum ick bekenne ontfanghen te hebben / end hier mede fijn all onse
reckeninghen doodt end te niet / end alles wat wy met malkanderen hadden
uytstaen voldaen Aldus ghedaen binnen Amsterdam ten huyse van A R in de

1646. D. F. G H.

A bill of lading after the Hollands manner.
I I P. of Amsterdam master under God of my ship called the Saint Peter, at
this present lying ready in the river of Amsterdam to sail with the first good
wind which God shall give toward London, where my right unlading shall be,
acknowledge and confess that I have received und r the ha^ches of my foresaid
ship of you S. I. merchaunt, to wit four pipes of oil, two chests of linen,
sixteen buts of Currents, one ball of carvase, five bals of pepper, thirteen
rings of brass wye^, fifty bar^ of iron, al dry and well conditioned marked
with this mark standing before. All which I promise to deliver (if God give me
a prosperous voyage with my foresaid ship) at London aforesaid to the
worshipful Mr. A I. to his facts of or assigns, paying for the freight of the
aforesaid goods 20 ss by the run. And for the performance of this before
written, I b^^d my self and all mine estates and my foresaid ship with all its
appurtenances.

In witness whereof I have signed three instruments hereof with my name or my
purser in my behalf, al of one contents, the one being performed the other to
be of no force. Written in Amsterdam the fifth day of September in the year
1646. I. P.

eersten goeden wint die Godt verlenen sal te se^len na London a^waer mijn

and upon the good ship called the Elli^ or of Pool, whereof is master under God
for this present voyage I. C, and now riding a^ anchor in the Mase, and by

Mr. I C and Mr. W W or to their assigns he or they paying straight for the sa
d goods according to custom with primage and avarage accustomed.

In witness whereof the master or purses of the said ship ha^h affirmed to three
bills of lading al of this tenor and date, the one of which three bills being
accomplished, the other two to stand void. And so God send the good ship to her
desired port in safety, Amen. Dated in Rotterdam 5 of September 1646. I C.

A table of the principal matters contained in this little book; by the help
whereof the scholar may find out any thing therein for his use either in the
learning of the matter or signification of words.

ab^eviation^ used in the Eng sh tongue. 3 O^ dip^^^ongs. 4 Of

nombers, and cases. 15 Of the noune ad^^ctive and i^ comparison. 18 Of the
pronoune and its several k^nds. 21 Of the verb and his conjugacion in all
moods, tenses, nombers, and persons. 24 Of the parts of speech that are
undeclinable, to wit, ad^^^. 31 Conjunction, preposition, and interjection. 32

Athanasi^s his creed. 44 9 The 35 and 39 chapters of Job, and a part of the 40

profitable for the for^derance of the scholar in the knowl dge of the tongues.

proverbiall) spe^ches, very pleasant to the mind, and profitable for the
